Local Tyrants from Hei Province Come to Harbin to Greet Zhang

Zhang Jinghui Still Not Showing Any Overt Signs

Japanese Army Pressuring the Hei Army Along the Qike Road

Harbin Correspondence - Ying Shun, the Deputy Director of the Special Police sent by Zhang Jinghui to Hei Province to administer the power, returned to Harbin yesterday morning (the 5th). Those who came with him included former Hei Province Police Chief Liu Dequan, Banner Army Commander Ji Xiang, and eighteen representatives of gentry and merchants. In the afternoon, Ying led them to see Zhang, asking Zhang to go to Hei Province immediately to preside over government affairs and organize the Heilongjiang Provincial Government. Zhang has not yet agreed to go. The representatives are still waiting for news in Harbin today. Yesterday, someone saw Zhang, and Zhang still said that he would never be a traitor and would not leave Harbin for Hei Province. However, Zhao Zhongren, who is running errands for Zhang, is still constantly threatening Ma Zhanshan in Hailun, demanding that he hand over the seals of office. Zhang's attitude is still not showing any overt signs. The guard team sent by Zhang to Hei Province had already begun to serve and maintain order, but a few days ago, the Japanese army in Hei Province, upon hearing rumors that Ma Zhanshan was planning to lead troops back to attack, fearing that the guard team would attack from both inside and outside the city, once confiscated their weapons. They were not returned until the day before yesterday. Currently, the Japanese army is especially concerned about a counterattack by the Hei army. They post sentries every night, guarding as far as a dozen miles around the city. After 7:00 PM, pedestrians are prohibited, and the police are closely inspecting the residents' household registration around the city, fearing that plainclothes soldiers from Ma's faction will enter the city. Most of the Japanese army's cavalry and artillery are successively arriving in Hei Province from the Jinxi area. Currently, the Japanese army is stationed along the Taoang Road Nenjiang Bridge all the way to Qiqihar city. Two armored trains have also been driven to Qiqihar and will be driven into the Qike Road. The three major camps in Hei Province, north, south, and east, are all full of Japanese troops, totaling more than 5,000 infantry, cavalry, and artillery. It is said that this unit belongs to the Suzuki Mixed Brigade. The army was opened from Hirosaki, Korea on the 14th of last month. The second division of Domen has been transferred back to Changji as a reserve force in the rear. Brigade Commander Suzuki arrived in Hei on the 6th of this month, and the Commander of the Kwantung Army, Honjo, commissioned him to be responsible for military affairs in Hei. The brigade began to advance along the Qike Road on the 5th, with more than 1,000 cavalrymen stationed at the Haoguantun post, taking a threatening stance against the Hei army. In addition, 500 cavalrymen are protecting dozens of workers dispatched by the South Manchuria Railway, advancing to the Tahar River, 45 li away from Ningnian Station, forcibly building a bridge over the river in preparation for advancing forward. It is rumored that there was a conflict between the two armies the night before last (the 4th), but it is not confirmed. On December 2nd, Ma Zhanshan took the head of the guard regiment, Xu Maizhen, and the commander of the first brigade of infantry, Yuan Chonggu, to the Keshantai'an area to deploy defenses. Because the artillery strength of each brigade team could not be united, they were specially concentrated into one regiment, compiled into the 55th regiment, and sent the chief of staff of the third brigade of infantry, Lieutenant Colonel Shi Lanbin, as the regimental commander, stationed in Lindian County, forming an angle with the defenses along the Maike Road line, in order to restrain the Japanese army when the opportunity arises for a counterattack. The number of young students from various places who came to join the army is very large. Ma has ordered them to be compiled into a training detachment and trained in Hailun. On the evening of the 3rd, Ma returned to the province. After hearing the news of the Japanese soldiers entering the province, he ordered the cavalry regiment stationed at the Tahar River to retreat to Ningnian, and contact the cavalry regiment to return to defense. Another envoy, Park Cheng, went to Keshan on the evening of the 5th to coordinate with the cavalry commander Zhi Zhiyuan to plan a strategy for resisting the enemy. Currently, Ma's intention is that an isolated army is trapped in a desperate situation. A rash counterattack will result in significant losses regardless of victory or defeat. Even if Hei Province is captured, the Japanese army will definitely counterattack with all its strength, and it will still be difficult to hold it. Therefore, at present, he is temporarily taking a wait-and-see attitude, actively replenishing the army's strength. Once the central government has a clear order to recover the lost territory, a large-scale mobilization will be carried out. If not, he fears that the current remnants will fight again in a hasty manner, and after retreating, there will be no way to salvage the situation. However, the Japanese army is afraid of Ma Zhanshan's counterattack, so it is using both threats and inducements. On the one hand, it is deploying troops from Qike Road to advance, taking on the appearance of an attack. On the other hand, Honjo sent his staff officer Sakatani and others to Harbin to persuade Zhang Jinghui to mediate with Ma, advising Ma to follow the method in Domen's previous letter, return to Hei Province to serve as the provincial chairman or garrison commander. Sakatani and others arrived in Harbin the day before yesterday, and Zhang Jinghui immediately contacted Ma Zhanshan by telephone. Ma said that he had no need to negotiate directly with the Japanese, and that the military and civilians in Hei Province were in high spirits. If the Japanese representative must come to Hailun to meet, there would be danger, and he would not be responsible. Seeing Ma's firm attitude, Sakatani dared not go to Hailun and is still in Harbin trying to persuade Ma by other means. As for Domen Sojiro, the commander of the Japanese Second Division who had previously led Ma to attack Hei Province, he has been transferred back to Liaoning. The day before he left, the local tyrants of Hei Province were extremely flattering and specially held a grand banquet to see him off. Domen, drunk, revealed that the Japanese army's attack on Hei Province this time was unexpected, and the losses were the heaviest since the occupation of the Northeast. His younger brother, a major general brigade commander, was killed in battle at Sanjianfang. Among the soldiers under his command who died, those who were not yet married numbered over 800, not including others. The words came from the mouth of the head of the beastly army, from which it can be known how bloody the Hei army was. (December 6th)

Legislative Yuan's Regular Meeting on December 12th

The Legislative Yuan held its 173rd general meeting from 8:00 AM to 12:00 PM on the 12th. Thirty-five members, including Luo Ding, attended. Shao Yuanchong presided over the meeting. The items for discussion were as follows: (1) The report of the Legal System Committee of this Yuan, reviewing the draft of the implementing rules for women's retroactive inheritance of property, resolved to adopt the review report; (2) The report of the Legal System Committee of this Yuan in conjunction with the Finance Committee, reviewing the procedures for the handover of officials upon leaving office, resolved to revise and pass the Civil Servants Handover Regulations; (3) The report of the Labor Law Drafting Committee of this Yuan, re-reviewing the draft of the Minimum Wage Law, resolved to adopt the review report; (4) The report of the Labor Law Drafting Committee of this Yuan, reviewing the draft amendments to Articles 13 and 16 of the Implementing Law of the Labor Union Law, resolved to amend and pass Articles 13 and 16 of the Implementing Law of the Labor Union Law.

He Siyuan Escorts School Principals to Beijing

Jinan Correspondence - In order to prevent students from various schools from going to Beijing to petition, Han Fuju ordered the Education Department the day before yesterday to suspend all expenses for schools participating in the petition from the date of the petition. However, this failed to stop the students from going south. The principals and teachers of various schools jointly submitted a letter of resignation to the Education Department yesterday. He Siyuan, the Director of the Education Department, immediately went to the Provincial Government to discuss solutions with Han Fuju. Han decided to stop the disbursement of funds there and not here. Since the students had already gone to Beijing, the funds would still be disbursed as usual. The secretariat of the Provincial Government immediately notified the Education Department and instructed the principals to stay in their positions. He said that the Ministry of Education had sent a telegram ordering him to escort the principals and responsible personnel of the petitioning schools to Beijing to help handle the student petitions. Han Fuju also firmly urged him to go. He specially accompanied the principals and responsible personnel, a total of sixteen people, to Beijing on the Pupu 201 train at 9:30 AM today (the 11th). However, the student special train was still stopped in Lincheng yesterday morning and did not arrive in Xu until late in the evening. It is still unknown whether it can go south. The actual number of students from various schools who went to petition is as follows: Women's Normal School 122, Women's Vocational School 3, Girls' Middle School 15, First Normal School 456, First Vocational School 64, First Rural Normal School 42, Qilu Middle School 50, Donglu Middle School 44, High School 525, Yuying Middle School 306, Zhengyi Middle School 297, Aimei Middle School 256, First Middle School 380, totaling 2,632 people. (December 11th)

Important News Two

A Part of Japan's Illegal Pending Cases (3)

The Case of the Massacre of Overseas Chinese During the Japanese Earthquake

During the great earthquake in Japan in September 1923 (Year 12 of the Republic of China), the Japanese took the opportunity to cruelly harm overseas Chinese. According to the investigation of the facts by the special envoy of our country, it can be divided into three items: (1) The case of the massacre of Chinese laborers in Oshima-cho. In the 1st to 8th Chome of Oshima-cho outside Tokyo City, there were more than 2,000 Chinese laborers. After the earthquake, Japanese self-defense corps, police, and soldiers induced the Chinese laborers to hand over all their money and forced them to the vicinity of the 8th Chome, where they were beaten to death with knives and sticks and the corpses were destroyed with kerosene to cover up the traces. The remaining Chinese laborers were transferred to barracks by the Japanese army for custody and then sent back to China. There is a Chinese person who recovered from death, as well as Japanese gentlemen and newspapers as evidence. (2) The case of the murder of student Wang Xitian. After the earthquake, Wang Xitian went around to provide relief to Chinese laborers. He suddenly disappeared in Tokyo on September 12. On that day, Japanese armed soldiers tied up Wang Xitian and detained him in the Kamedo Police Station in Tokyo. After that, his whereabouts were unknown. The Japanese side falsely claimed that he had been released, but he was undoubtedly murdered. There are Chinese people and the Salvation Army's memorial service on the same day as evidence. (3) The case of the murder of Chinese laborers and students in Yokohama and its vicinity. In Yokohama, in addition to the Chinese laborers who were killed, there were also three students who were killed. Two of them were witnessed by people being tied up and beaten by the Japanese self-defense corps with weapons until their heads were completely broken. The above facts were all committed by Japanese soldiers and police. It is clear that they were not accidental killings due to the chaos of the earthquake, and they all occurred after the day of the earthquake, and there is ample evidence. It is extremely difficult for Japanese officials to shirk responsibility. We have repeatedly sent notes to the Japanese ambassador and the Japanese Foreign Ministry, and sent lists of deaths, injuries, and damages, demanding that the murderers be punished and compensation be paid. However, they all made excuses to shirk responsibility and delayed the settlement of the case. It is estimated that 437 Chinese people were killed in this case, 46 were missing, 77 were injured, and property losses amounted to nearly 10,000 yuan.

Japan's Failure to Purchase Qingdao Salt According to the Agreement

According to the agreement on the details of resolving the Shandong pending cases, Japan should purchase a minimum of 100 million catties of Qingdao salt every year. However, since the establishment of the agreement, it has never complied with the quantity stipulated in the agreement. Even for the quantities that have been ordered, they are arbitrarily reduced midway. For example, 90 million catties were ordered in 1926 of the Republic of China, but 15 million catties were returned midway; 80 million catties were ordered in 1928, but 6 million catties were returned midway; 100 million catties were ordered in 1930, but 11.6 million catties were returned midway, causing the output and supply to lose their prepared standards. The agreement on the quantity and price of annual purchases is based on the unilateral opinion of the Japanese Monopoly Bureau, forcing the export managers to accept it, otherwise they are coerced by reducing the purchase quantity. Over the years, the export management companies have suffered significant losses. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has repeatedly approved the Ministry of Finance's request to negotiate with the Japanese side to handle the matter in accordance with the agreement, but there has been no result.

The First Korean Riot Case

In December 1927 of the Republic of China, Koreans, using the excuse of newspaper reports of the Eastern Provinces cracking down on Korean residents, gathered crowds to riot, insulting overseas Chinese, looting property, and besieging the Incheon Consulate, spreading to almost the entire Korean Peninsula. A total of two overseas Chinese died and 48 were injured. Direct losses amounted to more than 29,000 Japanese yen, and indirect losses amounted to more than 90,000 yuan. The Japanese ambassador took the opportunity to file a protest first, attempting to shirk responsibility for negligence. Our side refuted it and sent the number of deaths and injuries to the Japanese ambassador, demanding compensation. The compensation for the losses was pending investigation.

A statement was reserved, and after repeated urging to the Japanese Foreign Ministry, the matter was delayed with the excuse of transferring the investigation.

Cases of Japanese or Taiwanese Nationals Growing Drugs Under Real Names

Japanese or Taiwanese nationals use extraterritorial rights as a shield to openly open opium dens in China, such as Shanghai, Tianjin, Dalian, Liaoning, Beiping, Qingdao, Jinan, Hankou, Fuzhou, Xiamen, etc., or sell drugs such as morphine, cocaine, and heroin under the guise of practicing medicine and selling medicine, refusing to be cracked down by local civil affairs offices. The Japanese consulate even protests searches. After being caught on the spot, negotiations are held with the Japanese side, but the Japanese side always makes excuses to perfunctorily deal with the matter, always harboring protection and never achieving substantial results. The most notable cases include the following: (1) The case of the Dalian Japanese Exchange transporting heroin to Tianjin, Shenyang, Shijiazhuang, Jilin, and other places. The chairman of the Dalian Commodity Exchange colluded with a large number of Japanese to secretly transport drugs such as morphine, opium, and heroin. In 1928 of the Republic of China, the value was about 1.38 million Japanese yen. Before 1928, those discovered amounted to a huge sum of more than 4 million. Dalian was the central agency, and the drugs were transported to Tianjin, Shenyang, Shijiazhuang, Jilin, and other places. Those discovered and reported by the Procuratorate included Shirakawa, Yamamatsu, Uekama, Yano, and others. The matter involved the Tokyo and Dalian authorities and was widely reported in Dalian newspapers as one of the so-called five major mystery cases in Dalian. (2) The case of Japanese people manufacturing drugs in Hankou and transporting them to the interior. In February 1929, Japanese people manufactured morphine in Hankou using German machinery and sold it secretly. It was reported by the representative of the International Anti-Smoking Association. (3) The case of more than 100 Japanese merchants secretly selling drugs in Jinan City. Eight Japanese merchants in Jinan, including Kahoku Yoko's Inokari Toraji, Kaishun Pharmacy's Omori Shigeru, Choron Yoko's Kinai, Tairon Company's Ikoma Kiyoaki, Tenchi Yoko's Tajima Sadakazu, Gisei Yoko's Kiyoko Banzhichi, Jinan Company's Nonaka Kiyoji, and Yamaura Yoko's Yamaura Torao, have been manufacturing and selling various drugs for a long time. In August 1929, the Shandong negotiator, with the approval of the Shandong Provincial Government and the Public Security Bureau, dispatched police officers to investigate one by one and seized a large number of drug manufacturing raw materials and equipment on the spot, especially white pills. Our side sent a letter to the Japanese consulate in Jinan separately to seal up, punish, confiscate, and destroy them, but the results of the handling were not replied to. Other Japanese people residing in Jinan, Jiaozhou, Huantai, Weixian, Yidu, and other places who secretly sold drugs were also numerous. A separate list was also sent to the Japanese ambassador, but no reply was received. (4) The case of Japanese police forcibly demanding the opium offender Cui Yuanjun. When the Yanji Public Security Bureau searched Cui Yuanjun's home in Juzijie for an opium case in September 1929, the Japanese police suddenly intervened, and the request for negotiation was ineffective. (5) The case of the Japanese ship Changfeng Maru privately transporting opium. The Japanese ship Changfeng Maru loaded opium to Shanghai in November 1929. When it arrived at the Wusongkou, the Wusong Fortress Commander invited various French groups to check the ship's fire hold on the spot and seized a total of 20 cases of opium, about 300 taels. It was transferred to the Shanghai Court for interrogation and handled by the Anti-Smoking Committee, which sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to instruct the Jiangsu negotiator to negotiate with the Japanese consul in Shanghai for crackdown, but the Japanese consul did not reply. (6) The case of the Liaoning Post Office seizing drugs privately transported by Japanese Ii Haruji. In November 1929, the Liaoning Post Office seized more than 120 packages of heroin sent from Hamburg, Germany, each package priced at 500 taels. The recipient was Japanese Ii Haruji. After repeated verification by the Postal Bureau and the Liaoning Provincial Government, it was confirmed that the Japanese merchant himself admitted that it was heroin of the same nature. The provincial government burned it publicly and ordered the special envoy to negotiate for punishment and reported it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, according to letters from the German and Japanese ministers to strictly crack down. (7) The case of Fuzhou Japanese national Liao Xianzhang sheltering opium and leading the crowd to rob offenders. In December 1929, when the detective team cracked the opium case in the Pan Guan Miao, Fuzhou Japanese national Liao Xianzhang led the crowd to fire guns and hold knives to rob the opium offenders and escaped after shooting and injuring detectives and investigators, and has not been arrested. (8) The case of the Japanese garrison in Shanhaiguan forcibly demanding drug traffickers. The Japanese garrison in Shanhaiguan repeatedly forcibly demanded the return of drug traffickers arrested in Changli County. Nine Japanese families in Changli County used the name of practicing medicine and selling medicine, but in fact, they specialized in selling drugs such as morphine, cocaine, and heroin. The county's prohibition was ineffective. Whenever they were caught, they were demanded by the Japanese garrison. The Anti-Smoking Committee sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating that Changli was not a treaty port and Japanese people were not allowed to operate in the territory, and that their private sale of drugs was even more inappropriate. It requested the Japanese ambassador to inform the Japanese people not to stay in the county, but no reply was received. (9) The case of Japanese people selling drugs and military supplies in Gaomi County. Nine Japanese merchants in Gaomi County, including Kyoei Ten, Kanzawa, Maruyama, Mida, Takasho, Mishima, Kanaoka, and Kaneshiro, sold drugs and military supplies. The county government believed that Gaomi was not a treaty port and directly negotiated with them to ask them to leave the country, but they all refused strongly. The landlords repeatedly asked them to move out, but they also occupied the houses and refused to leave. Negotiations with the Japanese side also received no reply. (10) The case of more than 200 Japanese opium dens in Xiamen. Japanese Taiwanese residents Hong Rongbin, Zhou Falai, and Wang Nanbo and others opened opium dens and earth banks, defying the ban and delaying closure. In January 1930, there were still a total of 203 stores. The Siming County Government made a list and sent it to the Japanese consul in Xiamen for negotiation, but no results were obtained. There were even more in Fuzhou. (11) The case of the Qingdao Post Office detaining Japanese people privately transporting drugs. The Qingdao Japanese merchant Sanwa Shokai Yoshioka Yoko sold drugs and trafficked in cocaine and heroin from Switzerland and Hamburg, Germany, and sent them to Qingdao by registered mail through the post office, a total of 101 pieces. The Postal Inspection Office checked them, sent them to the Health Bureau for verification, confirmed that they were the above drugs, and submitted them to the Executive Yuan, which handed them over to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to request the Japanese ambassador to strictly crack down, but no reply was received. (12) The case of Fuzhou Japanese national shooting and killing opium smoker Lu Xi. In April 1930, Fuzhou Japanese national Xie Qingyun drew a pistol in a Taiwanese opium den in Houshou Baishe Temple and shot Lu Xi, a smoker, in the head. It went out from the back of the head, and he fell to the ground and died. The Fujian Provincial Government consulted with the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and sent a letter to the Japanese ambassador to request assistance in the arrest, but he has not been arrested. (13) The case of the Shanghai Customs detaining opium. In November 1930, the Shanghai Customs seized 100 boxes of opium on the German ship Klaus Rickmers. The cargo list only stated opium and was transferred from Shanghai to Dalian. The Customs detained it for violating customs regulations and confiscated it. In May of this year, the Japanese chargé d'affaires sent a letter to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, stating whether the fact that the Kwantung Government Monopoly Bureau ordered 100 boxes of opium from a Polish merchant and transported them to Dalian on the German ship Klaus Rickmers and were detained by the Shanghai Customs was true, and what was the reason. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs consulted with the Ministry of Finance to investigate and reply to the former situation, and then replied to the Japanese Embassy in Beiping. (14) The case of the Beiping Tadayoko selling military heroin. The Japanese merchant Arita Yoko in Xiaolisha Mao Hutong, Beiping, sold heroin. In December 1930, Xu Chunlin went to buy it. When he went out after buying it, he was caught by the police. Later, the Beiping Municipal Public Security Bureau found that there were 177 cases of Japanese people selling heroin, morphine, and other drugs in Beiping that had been cracked over the years, and they had been sent to the Japanese Embassy or the court for handling. (15) The case of Japanese people selling drugs in Hankou. Japanese Taniguchi Katsujiro sold poisonous water guns and poisonous liquid medicine in Hankou. In April 1931, the Gendarmerie Battalion seized them and sent the medicine together with a letter to the Municipal Hospital for verification. It was an aniline compound that could endanger human life. It was also tested on dogs, and the dogs lost consciousness. The entire case was transferred to the Municipal Government for handling. A total of five poison guns and fifty bottles of poison water (to be continued)

Valley Division's Artillery Shell Vehicle Explodes in Jinan

Jinan Correspondence: At about 2:00 PM today (9th), there was a sudden series of cannon explosions at Jinpu Railway Station, the sound shaking the roofs and tiles. Immediately, the military police tightened security around the station and prohibited pedestrians from passing. The cannon explosions stopped after half an hour and order was restored. It was found that a military artillery shell vehicle had exploded. The details of the incident are recorded as follows:

Origin of the Artillery Shells: The Ordnance Department of the 22nd Division of Valley Liangmin, which was suppressing bandits in southern Shandong, needed a large number of mortars and bullets. It sent staff member Yang Xirong, along with four ordnance officers and four soldiers, to Jinan to apply for them. The Ordnance Department of the Third Route Army, following the order of Commander-in-Chief Han Fuju, issued 300 rounds of 75mm mortar shells, 400 rounds of 82mm mortar shells, 500 infantry bombs, and 61,000 bullets. They were loaded onto a vehicle at 11:00 AM today, a covered 京奉 Railway forty-ton railway car, which was attached to the south-bound passenger train number 7 of the 津浦 Railway. There were many passengers on the train who had already purchased tickets and boarded, waiting to depart south (according to the scheduled time, it should have departed at 2:30 PM), unexpectedly, a tragic incident occurred temporarily.

Details of the Explosion: At 2:15 PM, while loading the vehicle, coolie Liu Xiaoquan and others were momentarily careless. While carrying a box of artillery shells onto the vehicle, they used too much force, causing it to fall over inside the vehicle. With a loud bang, a box of mortar shells exploded instantly, and the remaining artillery shells and bombs were also affected in succession. The sound was as dense as a string of pearls. People at the station and passengers in the vehicle fled in all directions. The vehicle was also destroyed. The station master's office, ticket office, north and south waiting rooms, section chief's office, telegraph room, baggage room, railway post office, and engineering department buildings all had broken glass and tiles. Artillery shells also landed inside the South Telegraph Administration Bureau of the station. For a time, people were inevitably panicked.

Rescue and Security: At that time, Zhou Shilian, the transport director of the Third Route Army stationed at the station, urgently telegraphed reports to various locations. The Public Security Bureau's fire brigade water trucks all set out to the station to put out the fire. Jinan Mayor Wen Chenglie, Garrison Commander Lei Taiping, and Public Security Bureau Chief Wang Kairu also rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm. Lei dispatched the second battalion of the second regiment of the pistol brigade to temporarily impose martial law around the station, completely cutting off pedestrians from the main road to the north and Guanzha Camp to the south to prevent danger. At that time, a freight train was conveniently stopped at the station. Station Master Wang Jingbo, fearing that it would be ignited, risked his life to move it away. After the incident, Jinan Mayor Wen Chenglie commended Wang for rescuing a train without avoiding danger and awarded him 200 yuan as an encouragement. By 4:30 PM, the explosions had stopped and the fire was extinguished. The security was lifted. Gun bullets and artillery shells were everywhere on the platform. The corpses of Song Huating, Liu Xiaoquan, Qiao Jide, and a child, who had been killed by the explosions, were still lying on the tracks, their flesh and blood blurred, a tragic sight.

Number of Casualties: After investigation, a total of four people were killed by the explosions, including Jinan Station coolies Qiao Jide and Liu Xiaoquan, and Song Huating, a major regimental adjunct of the Liang Guanying unit of the 25th Route Army, and an unnamed child, reportedly the daughter of an ordnance officer of the artillery regiment of the 29th Division. The Public Security Sub-bureau of the Southwest Township dispatched personnel to provide coffins for them. A total of eleven people were injured, including Yao Zhishan and Wei Zonghan, captains of the 64th regiment of the 22nd Division, Chen Wencai, a platoon leader of the machine gun company of the 3rd regiment of the 66th Brigade, and Wang Jiazhen, a nurse at the army hospital of the artillery regiment of the 29th Division, who were sent to the Third Route Army Hospital for treatment by Guan Shilian, the director of the Third Route Army's station office. Coolie Liu Ershang, Ruan Liangchen, Gao Wenguang, driver Guan Huaming, messenger Zhang Shaokang of the 25th Route Army, and cook Chen Caijun were all sent to the Jinpu Railway Hospital for treatment by Station Master Wang.

Authorities' Investigation: Yang Xirong, the staff member of the Ordnance Department of the 22nd Division who came to Jinan to apply for artillery shells, disappeared after the incident. Fu Zhengde, the director of the Ordnance Department of the 22nd Division, had already taken a train south from Jinan to his defense area today. Upon hearing that the bullet vehicle had caused an accident at Baimashan Station, he rushed back to Jinan to investigate the situation. Liu Kewen, the director of the Ordnance Department of the Third Route Army, also arrived at the scene of the accident to jointly investigate. (December 9th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Opening of Ballots for the Election of the Chinese Medicine Association

The Songjiang County combined and organized the Chinese Medicine Association, and held an inaugural meeting on October 20. After the election, the ballots could not be opened, as reported in the previous newspaper. Delayed until December 4, the county party department sent a committee member Xu Xinmin to guide, and the county government sent a committee member Zhu Zhangqi to supervise, convening members of the Chinese Medicine Association to open the ballots in the county party department's auditorium. As a result, Huang Songxian and eight others were elected as executive committee members, Zhang Jinshan and two others were elected as alternate executive committee members, Xia Zhongfang and four others were elected as supervisory committee members, and Wu and Fu were elected as alternate supervisory committee members. After the ballots were opened, representatives such as Zha Gongfu were selected from the members of the Chinese Medicine Association to notify the elected candidates. The executive committee members immediately elected Huang Songxian, Cao Boyin, and Wu Guochao as standing members, and Huang Songxian was elected as the standing chairman. A document has been prepared and submitted to the county party department and the county government to send committee members to receive it.

Danyang

Diantou Township Robbed

The home of farmer Liu Ruiqi in Diantou Township, Ninth District, was suddenly attacked by more than ten bandits the day before yesterday. They rushed into the house, searched and looted extensively, and robbed Liu's self-defense gun.

Four Bandits Captured

The chief of the Lucheng Public Security Sub-bureau, while patrolling yesterday, saw four suspicious-looking people drinking tea in a certain teahouse. He immediately stepped forward to question them, but they stammered. Two Browning pistols and many bullets were found on their persons. They were immediately taken to the bureau for preliminary interrogation. According to their statements, they are named Wang Qiren, Zhang Alin, Peng Qing, and Zhu Zhong. Their attitude was stubborn and they refused to tell the truth. They were immediately escorted to the county government by the police. Yesterday, Judge He conducted a secret trial and admitted to robbing Changgou Village once. Bandit Peng also confessed to joining the Communist Party. The remaining confessions were evasive. They have now been detained awaiting trial.

Zhenjiang

Representatives from All Circles Go to Beijing Today to Petition

Representatives from all circles in the province held a meeting at the National Salvation Association yesterday to discuss matters related to petitioning in Beijing. More than ten representatives from various groups and schools attended. Chairman Liu Yusheng decided that they would gather at the National Salvation Association at 1:00 PM this Sunday to depart. Each group and school will send one to three representatives and pay a membership fee of five yuan. Liu Yusheng was elected as commander, and Wang Jinshan, Tao Shoubai, Jiang Xiaochen, and Ye Zuoren were elected as spokespersons.

Thorough Investigation of the Jinghang Road Embezzlement Case

The Provincial Party Department yesterday sent another letter to the Provincial Government to thoroughly investigate the Jinghang Road embezzlement case. The original letter stated, "With the approval of the Provincial Supervisory Committee's letter, the Jinghang Highway Engineering Office embezzlement case has not yet been resolved. It has recently been reported that the detainees have been released on bail one after another, causing public outcry. As it is the duty of this association, we cannot remain silent. Therefore, it was resolved at the tenth meeting of this association to send a letter to the executive committee at the same level, which will forward the letter to the Provincial Government, requesting a prompt and thorough investigation, and requesting the case to be transferred to the Supervisory Yuan to settle the accounts of the office. The corresponding record has been sent to you in a letter, hoping that you will investigate and handle it."

Sentence of Imprisonment for Fraudulent Acquisition of Wealth

Bai Chengye, Sun Shuxi, and others, former staff members of the Anti-Japanese Association who were dismissed, were reported for privately inspecting stores under the name of the Anti-Japanese Association, attempting to fraudulently obtain wealth. After investigation, it was confirmed. The Anti-Japanese Association transferred the case to the court, which filed a public prosecution with the Criminal Court, requesting that they be sentenced for jointly defrauding wealth. Judge Zhou interrogated them yesterday. Bai and Sun claimed that the inspection procedures were merely incorrect and that there was no request for wealth. After verifying the confessions, Judge Zhou, based on the fact that the facts of the crime had been investigated and clarified by the Anti-Japanese Association, sentenced them to one year of imprisonment each in court.

Yangzhou

Students and Businesses Strike and Conduct Anti-Japanese Demonstrations in the City

All middle schools in Yangzhou Province went on strike on the 11th. At 10:00 AM, 3,000 students gathered at the public stadium and formed a line to parade, holding anti-Japanese demonstrations. They chanted anti-Japanese slogans along the way. All the stores in the city, in accordance with the resolutions of the joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees of the Chamber of Commerce and the representatives of the trade associations at 4:00 PM on the 10th, strictly severed economic ties with Japan. They all closed the city on the 11th. At 10:00 AM, they all gathered at the County Chamber of Commerce and set off in a line, led by Chairman Wang Jingtian, to parade through the streets, chanting slogans to express their determination to resist Japan and to be the government's backing. They also telegraphed the National Government, the Central Party Department, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs, stating that diplomacy was like this, national affairs were like this, and the violent Japanese were also like this. They could only urgently implore their government to lead the nation's long-fighting soldiers to expel the national traitors. The situation was critical and urgent. The Yangzhou merchants went on strike for one day to show their support for the government. They respectfully telegraphed this.

Resolutions of the Anti-Japanese Executive Committee Meeting

The Jiangdu County People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association held a re-election on the 9th. At 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the 10th, the executive committee meeting was held and Zhu Zhusun and Tang Shou were elected to take over all matters of the association. Fourteen articles on the method of sealing up Japanese goods were also passed. In the future, if suspected goods are found, they must be inspected in Shanghai. One person from the association, the Chamber of Commerce, and the purchasing store will be sent to Shanghai for re-inspection. It was decided to gather at the public stadium at 9:00 AM on the 12th to seal up Japanese goods in various stores with students from the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association, and to discuss the method of sealing up Japanese goods after 3:00 PM on the 15th.

Jiaxing

Capture of Bandit Spy

The seventh team of the Jiaxing County Merchants' Voluntary Security Corps found a suspicious person on the Tanghui Tiedong the night before last. He was carrying a weapon and spoke with an Eastern Township accent. According to him, someone had arranged to wait here, preparing to rob a certain family on the opposite side of the Eastern Zha River, and also invited the God of Wealth. The team immediately reported to the corps headquarters and the public security organs dispatched a team to set up defenses. Sure enough, at midnight, a boat from Eastern Township came from the east. The team members ordered it to stop, but the boat sailed very quickly and escaped. Yesterday, the bandit spy was escorted to the corps headquarters by the team and sent to the Public Security Bureau, which transferred him to the court for investigation.

Student Union Sends a Letter Urging the Director of the Education Bureau to Resign

The student unions of various middle schools in Jiaxing sent a letter on the 11th to Shen Da, the director of the County Education Bureau, urging him to resign voluntarily because he had repeatedly obstructed the anti-Japanese work and suppressed the students' patriotic movement. They also petitioned the county government. It is now learned that Director Shen has resigned to the superior government after receiving the letter and has also sent a letter to the student unions to inform them.

Huzhou

Clarification of Pawnshop Handling Fees

According to the request of the All Zhejiang Pawn Industry Association to clarify the management handling fees and retain the original storage box fees, the Provincial Construction Department stated that there was nothing inappropriate about the requested clarification of the management handling fees. However, the original storage box fees had been stipulated to be abolished, and the requested retention should not be discussed. It is now approved that the handling fee should not exceed 5/1000th of the fixed price per month at most and must comply with the provisions of Article 12 of the Revised Zhejiang Province Pawn Business Provisional Rules and other two items. After being submitted by the county government to the Provincial Construction Department for approval, it can be charged. The association is instructed to comply and report to the Provincial Government for record, and the Wuxing County Government is instructed to comply.

Ningbo

Sandboat Encountered Robbers

The Xu Shuntai large sandboat can carry more than 200 tons and has more than 20 crew members. The captains are Chen Jinquan and Shi Fushou from Dinghai. On the 4th of this month, it loaded 2,500-600 pieces of passenger goods, redwood, and seafood worth more than 30,000 yuan from Fuzhou to Yong. Unexpectedly, at 5:00 PM on the 7th, while traveling through the Jinmen Island waters near Taizhou Bay, it was suddenly intercepted by three pirate ships. The captains tried their best to escape, but the pirates opened fire. The boat was hit by more than 20 bullets, and crew members Cao Asheng and Li Aquan were each hit by one bullet. They had no choice but to stop the boat. More than 100 pirates swarmed onto the boat to rob, searching the crew members for more than 200 yuan and robbing more than 900 pieces of redwood and seafood. They carried them over to the ship and first loaded one ship. The remaining two pirates still held the sandboat, forcing the captains to redeem the boat and all the crew members for 25,000 yuan. The captains pleaded repeatedly, but could not be exempted. At 5:00 AM on the 8th, a small sailboat passed by. The pirate leader ordered crew member He Yuesheng to take the sailboat to Yong to report and set a deadline to prepare the money for redemption within the year. Crew member He Yuesheng arrived in Zhenhai yesterday morning and reported the encounter to the cargo owners. In the afternoon, he transferred to a steamboat to Dinghai to report to the captains' families and find ways to rescue them.

Farmhouse Robbed, Loss of More Than 1,000 Gold

Zheng Jicun, a farmer in Gaochetou, Yin County, is a wealthy household in the area. At midnight yesterday, seven bandits suddenly came with weapons and broke open the back door with stones to enter and plunder wantonly. They robbed sixteen gold rings, four gold diamonds, six pairs of gold earrings, eight gold hairpins, six or seven leather clothes, etc., with a loss of more than 1,000 gold.

Local News

Zheng Hongnian Issues Statement

Students' Patriotic Movement is Premier's Legacy

University Students Discussing Politics Already Existed in the Autocratic Era

Due to the current national crisis, the universities in this city have petitioned in Nanjing twice. The students of Jinan University, elected by the Student Union, are in command. The Central Government inevitably suspects Zheng Hongnian. Yesterday, the Western newspapers reported that Nanjing ordered the Shanghai Garrison Command to secretly arrest Zheng. Whether this is true or not is unknown. The reporter went to visit Zheng to inquire about the situation. Zheng said that the enthusiastic performance of young students is actually a good phenomenon. However, education politicians speculate with vile intentions, stirring up trouble to curry favor, causing resentment among young people, and giving a major lesson to those who use young people as tools, which is deeply regrettable. I have always held the principle of running education for the sake of education, and I never use students as tools. I have repeatedly told this to my students. Precisely because I do not use students as tools, students are able to rise up automatically in times of crisis. This has many precedents in various countries. Even in our country, in the autocratic era, Li Ying exemplified the Imperial Academy in the Han Dynasty, and Chen Dong knelt before the palace gates to submit memorials in the Song Dynasty, refusing to be bowed by authority and unafraid of slander by petty men. The morale of the scholars was very high, and history praised them as men of integrity. University students discussing court politics is not new in history. This patriotic movement by students from various schools is also the legacy of Premier Sun to restore the inherent spirit of the nation. Currently, it is the preliminary stage of expressing the restoration of the national spirit. The actions and steps of the students may not be consistent. This is a phenomenon that should occur during a period of transition. Guiding the situation to promote strengths and correct shortcomings is what those of us who run education should strive for. As for the pure and patriotic actions of our school's students, it is not unreasonable to say that it is due to my usual effective education. It is truly an expression of good educational results, and I personally feel very comforted. China will not perish because of this. Confucius said, "If, on examination, I find that I am upright, what is there to worry about? What is there to fear?" I repeat these words to myself three times a day.

Shanghai Municipal Council Decides to Add Chinese Schools

(Shenshi News Agency) Regarding the addition of Chinese schools in the Shanghai Municipal Council's education plan, at the meeting of the Education Committee on December 2nd, the chairman stated that according to the council's established plan, two new schools should be added each year. However, only one school was established in 1931. The Director of Public Works responded that the key to this matter lies in finding suitable school sites. The Education Committee should determine the required number of sites so that the Public Works Department can investigate and design. Although two schools could not be established this year, the council has leased two sites for use.

The chairman then read a letter from the Chinese members, stating that because two primary schools and one girls' secondary school may not be added next year, they suggested temporarily renting houses to establish two coeducational primary schools, and allocating part of the funds originally designated for building permanent school sites to the 1932 budget, so that construction could begin in 1932 and be completed in 1933. The chairman also stated that the council's education plan must be implemented as much as possible in the initial years.

One member stated that since the committee plans to build as many as sixteen new schools, the distance between the schools may be very far. The Director of Public Works responded that he intended to find a site in the industrial area of the Western District, but this would also depend on the financial situation. The chairman then proposed that the Director of Public Works immediately begin investigating which buildings could be rented in order to add two Chinese primary schools in 1932. This proposal was passed.

One member stated that he did not oppose the temporary measure of renting houses to establish schools, but he should solemnly declare that the committee was forced to do so. Building permanent school buildings is extremely important, so he strongly supported finding about six plots of land as permanent primary school sites, and paying special attention to the Western District. After an investigation report is received, funds will be allocated in the 1932 budget to purchase this land.

The Director of Finance then mentioned the need to save expenses, but the general opinion was that the Education Department's position was different from other departments. Since the council had decided to change its education policy and establish more schools for the Chinese, it would be a breach of faith to the Chinese residents if this policy were violated.

One member then proposed a compromise, which was to find one or more plots of land in the Eastern District to build temporary school buildings in order to avoid the huge rent of renting houses. The consensus was that if school buildings could not be rented at a reasonable price, this proposal could also be considered for reference.

Jinan and Donghua Struggle Bitterly in Bone-Chilling Wind to a Draw

Grade A Football Match

The weather suddenly turned cold, and the wind was bone-chilling. The Donghua and Jinan football teams still held the Grade A treasure at the China Baseball Field yesterday. After 90 minutes of fierce battle, the result was a score of zero to zero, with neither side scoring. Given the strength of Donghua and Jinan, and their first encounter, three or four thousand people still braved the cold to watch, shivering but unyielding.

The Generals on Both Sides are Refreshed

The generals on both sides have undergone changes, especially Jinan. The injured are injured, and the sick are sick. The main generals Jiang Shanjing and Luo Haiguang, and the goalkeeper Wen Dingxin, did not play. Even Qiu Dongyan, a key player in the forward line, was reassigned to the defense. Donghua was also missing the central forward Dai, who had a mission of command, and Chen Jiaqiu was promoted to replace him.

Performance in the Wind is Difficult

The north wind roared, blowing against faces and swirling people around. It was unbearable to be in the cold, let alone kick against the wind. When Donghua first faced the wind, the ball could not be kicked out, and the activity changed as usual. Kicking the ball was also not as desired, and the performance was not worth mentioning. The Donghua defense is not worth mentioning. The central defense line was very good yesterday, the new Jin, the veteran Chen, and the midfielder Tu were all very satisfactory. Among the forwards, Qian Jingyong was very active. Feng Yunyou in Jinan was heavily burdened in the back, defending all sides. Qiu Dongyan was also quite good, showing that he could attack and defend. The forward Xiao Heitan was monitored by others, so his activities were not often seen.

Jinan's Momentum Was Terrifying

Referee Li Nuosi, Donghua kicked off, and Jinan took advantage of the wind to launch a large-scale invasion. Chen Fuzhong passed to Mei Hongbao, who rushed along the side, creating a corner kick. Mei Hongbao's corner kick was excellent, but Yang Baomiao failed to kick it well, which was a pity. Only two minutes into the game, Donghua got the ball, Chen Pu and Qian Jingyong also rushed forward, passing to Chen Yutian. The shot was very light, and Chen Buzhang caught it and kicked it out. Jinan then led the team to attack again. Liang Shutang shot from more than 30 yards away, and Zhou Xianyan kicked it out smoothly. Both were surrounded and attacked, and the head was actually kicked, fortunately without serious harm. The first half ended like this.

Injustice for Jiaqiu Who Did Not Turn Against His Team

Some people blamed Chen Jiaqiu for Donghua's repeated failures to score, suspecting that since Chen was originally from Jinan, replacing the center forward was suspicious. Therefore, some called Jiaqiu a traitor. In fact, it was an injustice. Please look at the facts. After Donghua changed sides, its momentum increased sharply, and it also launched attacks. Unfortunately, the two free kicks 20 yards in front of the goal were not scored, one by Li Yichen and one by Ma Kaiyuan. Suddenly, the reporter's incident was discovered. Chen Jiaqiu dribbled the ball, charging straight on horseback, breaking through three levels in a row, and shooting fiercely at the goal. It was thought that it would go in, but the ball happened to hit Chen Buzhang's hand and was blocked. How did Jiaqiu turn against the team? After another 20 minutes of hard fighting, the final score was 0-0.

Two Special Books on Basketball

(1) "Basketball Training Method" by Wu Bangwei

(2) "Basketball Refereeing Method" Translated by Peng Wenyu

The "Sports Series" published by the Qinfen Bookstore at Huajinlikou, Sima Road, Shanghai, is written by famous sports figures across the country. It comprehensively covers sports theory and sports technology. The content of each volume is excellent and meets modern needs, and has been praised by the Minister of Education, department heads, provincial and municipal education directors, and sports groups. Among this series, "Basketball Training Method" and "Basketball Refereeing Method" are particularly popular. Many basketball players and coaches have one copy in hand. "Basketball Training Method" is written by Wu Bangwei, a current professor of physical education at National Central University and director of the Jiangsu Provincial Public Sports Field. Mr. Wu has more than ten years of experience in guiding basketball training. The book is divided into seven chapters, detailing the training of basic basketball techniques, the cultivation of players, and the methods of joint defense and offense, and the organization of the team. Each basic movement is accompanied by photos taken by the author himself demonstrating the correct posture. Each offensive and defensive method is accompanied by illustrations, arranged in a formation, and indicating the steps. There are also more than 30 special diagrams for free throws, out-of-bounds balls, and kick-offs. Readers can easily observe. Each volume is priced at 90 cents, now at a special price of 90% off. An additional 7 cents is added for mailing by letter. Another book, "Basketball Refereeing Method," is compiled and translated by Peng Wenyu, a physical education instructor at Northeastern University. The book is divided into 11 chapters. In addition to explaining the qualifications, ethics, and various refereeing methods of basketball referees, it also thoroughly explains the preparation for the game, the method of controlling the field, and the latest dual referee system. All basketball referees should not be without this book for a day, and even players should read it carefully to avoid fouling in the field. Each volume is priced at 60 cents, now at a special price of 90% off. Add 7 cents for mailing by letter. The main table of contents of the two books is as follows:

(1) "Basketball Training Method" Chapter 1: Brief introduction to basketball game; Chapter 2: Basic basketball techniques; Chapter 3: Joint defense method; Chapter 4: Joint offense method; Chapter 5: Special formation diagram; Chapter 6: Organization and management of basketball team; Chapter 7: Training of basketball team; (2) "Basketball Refereeing Method" Chapter 1: Qualifications of basketball referees; Chapter 2: Preparation before the game; Chapter 3: Method of controlling the field; Chapter 4: Method of cooperating with inspectors; Chapter 5: Responsibility of inspectors; Chapter 6: Procedure for announcing fouls; Chapter 7: Rest time; Chapter 8: Dual referee system; Chapter 9: Referees and spectators; Chapter 10: Ethics of referees; Chapter 11: Summary of basketball refereeing method.

Page 15

Free Talk

Recollections of the Tortoiseshell Beam

— Yanzi

In our nation's art circles, those painters and calligraphers who have frequent interactions with famous figures from the East and are highly regarded in that country include Qian Shoutie, Wang Yiting, Ma Qizhou, Sun Xueni, and Ma Mengrong. Wang earns about ten thousand taels of silver annually from Japanese commissions, and people in Japan consider it an honor to possess even a small piece of his work. Since the Japanese army occupied Liaoning and Jilin, Wang has resigned from his position as a comprador for Japanese companies to show his resolve. Qian Shoutie's rustic calligraphy and paintings are highly valued by the Japanese, but Qian, being of a proud nature, rarely grants requests. Recently, he refused a request from the Japanese and, along with Sun Xueni, Ma Mengrong, Ma Qizhou, and others, is assisting Madam He Xiangning in a charity art exhibition to aid in national salvation. They are soliciting paintings and running around appealing to people, tears flowing as they speak, demonstrating that their patriotic fervor has reached a boiling point. Ma Mengrong painted "Strange Fish" and two paintings titled "Even a Barbarian Is Not as Good as a Crab," adding long, impassioned poems that satirize the abilities of the Japanese pirates. Those who saw them were moved to smash their spitoons in anger. Sun Xueni used to have dealings with Japanese merchants, but since the Northeast Incident, he has severed all business ties with them. He He Tianjian inscribed a set of anti-Japanese calendars and distributed them to his friends. The paintings were exquisitely rendered by his talented student, Tian Qingquan. He Tianjian's inscriptions were profound in thought and expression, serving as lasting memorials. Most remarkably, Ma Qizhou engaged in poetic exchanges with the Japanese poet Tanaka Keinan, sending poems back and forth through the postal system. Last month, Tanaka sent another poem to Ma, to which Ma replied with a letter of severing ties, including the lines, "With national enmity forged, national humiliation must not be forgotten. Let us sever ties from this day forth. We shall meet amidst gunfire and bullets. Do not say that there is no one left in Qin." Currently, he is launching the "Four Ma Support Ma Art Exhibition" with Ma Wanli, Ma Mengrong, and Ma Gongyu to sell paintings to support military expenses, which has been lauded by those who have heard of it.

Great Revelations from the Bu Chu Ting Cao Studio

Opening Remarks of a Historical Drama

Shakespeare said, "The world is a stage..." Humanity is staging an unprecedented historical drama, and both those who are too lazy to move and those who are happy to move are characters in the play. I cannot write a script, so let a clown sing a few opening lines:

"I too once made revolution,

Now too lazy to move, afraid of others moving.

Should anyone dare to move,

I will denounce them as reactionaries!"

(1) A gardener's responsibility is to irrigate, fertilize, and remove pests, not to confiscate the seedlings' free air and sunlight... (Ding mistaken for Zhong)

Records of Customs and Scenery of Longjiang by Ma Shichi

My friend, Mr. Wang Beiming, is renowned in the legal field and particularly enthusiastic about the anti-Japanese cause. The "Five-Man National Salvation Group" was initiated by him. Recently, he returned from the Shanghai Special District Court and visited me by car. We talked late into the night, and he told me about the customs and scenery of Longjiang, giving me a general idea. He had served in the Heilongjiang government. Alas, with Ban Dingyuan not appearing, and Qi Shaobao deceased, I looked out at our rivers and mountains, half of which have fallen into foreign hands. I record this article, my ink mixed with tears, unable to bear the feeling of national loss.

Heilongjiang was known as North Fuyu and the land of the various Wuji tribes during the Northern Wei Dynasty. During the Tang Dynasty, the Shiwei and Mohe tribes arose there. When the Manchus entered the Pass, they built cities in Heilongjiang and established generals and commanders-in-chief to guard them. In the late Qing Dynasty, the generals were dismissed, and governors were appointed. Prefectures, departments, and counties were established, and the provincial government was set up in Qiqihar (transliteration), known as Longjiang Prefecture. After the establishment of the Republic of China, the government was organized into counties, but Qiqihar remained the provincial capital.

Qiqihar is a small place, with city walls facing each other. One can see the west gate from the east gate. The city is narrow and cramped, with camels and mule carts for transportation. Outside the city, there are fertile fields and abundant livestock. The people are hardworking and accustomed to farming, unlike the extravagance and effeminacy of the South. However, their farming methods are conservative and unchanging. Seeds are scattered freely in the fields, without irrigation or mounds. When it is time to harvest, the dregs are used for food, while the best grains are sold overseas. Their daily sustenance consists of wheat, made into a flour mixed with soil, coarse and black as charcoal, seasoned with salt, so bitter that it is almost impossible to swallow. But the people of Heilongjiang regard it as a rare delicacy. How influential are customs!

The land of Heilongjiang is extremely cold. The river freezes in August and does not thaw for eight months. Rainfall is scarce. In autumn, the rain and dew turn to ice and snow. Mules and horses trample it, leaving manure on the snowy ground that freezes and does not melt, causing hardship for travelers. The outskirts are unbearably cold. Sometimes, tears and snot freeze, making it difficult to open one's eyes. Lambskin is the only way to keep warm in Heilongjiang. A robe requires only ten or so sheep. However, the style of clothing is strange, with the wool facing outward and lined with coarse cloth. The leather boots and face covers are also made this way. I do not know what purpose this serves. The houses are airtight and free from moisture. In winter, residents build heated brick beds (kangs) to keep warm. Fuel is scarce, so they use dried mule and horse manure. The kang is fitted with a pipe that vents outside, preventing foul odors. Entering a home is like returning to spring in a millet field.

Plants sprout in early summer and wither in early autumn. The period of growth is very short. Watermelons are produced in July and must be eaten wrapped in cotton. In the height of summer, June is best for wearing light clothing, but traveling in the suburbs in the early morning or late evening is still chilly.

The climate of Heilongjiang is unique, and the transition from morning to evening is almost the opposite of that in the South. In spring and summer, the days are short and the nights are long. In autumn, the opposite is true. Near the winter months, it is dark most of the time, usually by 9:30.

The main agricultural products are soybeans and wheat, followed by vegetables such as lettuce and radishes. The soybean crop has been particularly abundant in recent years. However, transporting it to the interior is very expensive, and taxes are heavy, leading to a loss. As a result, there is overproduction, and some is destroyed and used as fuel, which is a great pity. I hope that those who advocate promoting domestic products will consider this.

Mr. Wang also said that the northeastern provinces are often referred to as "barren land and poor people." In reality, the people are indeed poor, but the land is not barren. If cultivation can be improved, animal husbandry diligently practiced, mineral resources developed, and transportation improved, prosperity can be achieved in less than ten years, and production can be sufficient for the entire country. This is what the Japanese invaders seek day and night, seizing by trickery and force. How can we, the descendants of the Yellow Emperor, inherit such mountains and rivers and abandon them to our descendants? How can our descendants fear difficulty and live in ease, handing them over under the doctrine of non-resistance?

Anecdotes of General Li Fangchen

— Shi Lei'an

General Li Jinglin, director of the Central Guoshu Academy and a veteran general of the Northern Warlords, recently passed away from rectal bleeding. When the news arrived, people at home and abroad, whether they knew him or not, mourned his death. In particular, Li's old friends and subordinates cried until they lost their voices.

Li, named Fangchen, was from Zaoqiang, Hebei Province. He was forty-seven years old. He came from a poor family and lost his father early. When he came of age, he had great ambitions. He studied in Japan and graduated from the Military Academy. After returning to China, he rose rapidly from battalion commander to prominent positions. Marshal Zhang Zuolin valued him most and repeatedly gave him important tasks, such as military commander, superintendent, and commander-in-chief. Li governed his troops with strictness, comparable to Marquis Wen. The people of the Northeast still praise him today.

Many military men in our country possess vast wealth, but Li alone did not engage in production. After the Northern Expedition, he severed all ties with fame and fortune. The authorities, knowing his ability, wanted to station him in a certain area, but Li firmly declined. Instead, he took up the post of director of the Central Guoshu Academy, where he made many plans for the development of martial arts. His contribution to promoting national essence and strengthening the people cannot be denied.

In his later years, Li indulged in Chan Buddhism and had thoughts of transcending the world. One day, he said to his wife, "I am old and have wasted many years, serving in the military for many years. I am ashamed to have achieved nothing for the people. Now that our children have grown up and can support themselves, how can I abandon the mortal world and escape like Wu Ziyu to the outside world?" After speaking, he looked pensive. His calligraphy was elegant and strong, similar to that of Yu Shinan. I once saw a couplet he wrote for He Jiajun: "The horse neighs in the stable like Zhi Dun; the pond raises geese like Wang Xizhi." The brushstrokes were powerful, revealing a heroic spirit. According to Li's staff, the general lived a frugal life and enjoyed reading and swordsmanship. He was naturally gifted with a strong physique. However, in recent years, he suffered from rheumatism from years of campaigning, and his hands and feet often felt sore and numb. The doctor advised him to take beef juice regularly to dispel the disease and strengthen his body. Li then ordered several dozen bottles of Colworth's beef juice from the market. It proved to be remarkably effective.

A Short Record of Strange Fish

— Zheng Yimei

Fish swim in water and enjoy themselves. The Buddhist term "water shuttle flower" is derived from this. There are many kinds of fish, but only one-tenth of them are used for cooking. Here, I record strange fish I have heard of and seen in books, hoping to amuse readers.

Yunnan has crystal fish. The fish's intestines and stomach are translucent, allowing one to see clearly inside.

Flying fish, also known as Wenyao fish, are found along the coast of the United States. They are one and a half to one and a half feet long, with a dark blue back and a white belly. The scales are round, large, and easily shed. They swim in schools on the surface of the sea. The pectoral fins are large, sometimes larger than the body, and are used as wings to fly over the water surface, reaching a height of six or seven feet.

The Zhuhuai River contains the Yiyu fish. It has the body of a fish and the head of a dog.

Records of Things Seen and Heard in the Old Capital

— Zhu An

Yellow Bud Cabbage

The north has early frosts and deep cold, making it suitable to eat vegetables that can't be had during winter. Yet, it is actually the contrary. Yellow bud cabbage is the product of a rich frost that makes it both succulent and delicious. In the spring, it becomes bland and tasteless. This is called frost cabbage. With the stove fire lit, a bowl of cooked vegetables and a soup accompaniment will be an additional treat. No meat flavor is needed. It can be eaten daily without boredom, so it is a superior vegetable. If pickled in a jar with salt, weighed down with a stone, and frozen, it crunches like ice. This must be the salt pickles Su Dongpo enjoyed after drinking. In the past, the Manchus mixed rare fruits and grains into porridge on the eighth day of the twelfth month, called Laba porridge. Friends exchanged gifts, with these pickles being the most prized. The quality of the vegetable can predict a family's prosperity. In the cold season, northern people burn coal balls for heating. In poor homes, the windows are small and tightly sealed. When the coal fire is dying, it produces poisonous fumes. People sleep unaware and suffocate to death. In the past, there was no western medicine for emergency treatment. Drinking pickle juice was the only way to revive them. All families had it. In recent years, western-style stoves are used. Even if coal balls are still used, people know to move the dying fire outside before going to bed. The police also have medicines and give advice. This problem is becoming rare. Those who are new to the northern capital should inquire and be careful. There are also greenhouses in the north where vegetables can be grown artificially. Thus, in the severe cold of ice and snow, if one wants to eat cucumbers, one can have them immediately, but the price is expensive.

The Sound of Selling Ice

Shu Wei's Bingshuizhai Collection has a poem about sending to the family in Beijing: "Lilacs and peonies have all bloomed, apricots and cherries are gradually becoming cheaper. The sound of golden shears just stopped the copper bowl rings, the sound of selling flowers has turned to the sound of selling ice." This poem vividly describes the scenery of summer. Ice sellers make sounds by hitting two copper bowls together. It's convenient and clear. It can be found in many notes by the people of Ming and Qing. This tradition is very old. Now, not only ice sellers but also dessert sellers do this. Ice for sale in the northern capital is mostly stored in the Ten Temples Sea. In winter, ice is chiseled out of the sea in large blocks and stored in caves. They're released and sold in the summer of the following year. Everyone, rich or poor, uses them freely. The policy of storing and distributing ice was very important in ancient times. The previous dynasty still had a custom of giving ice in April to reduce the troubles of the hot weather, which is like following the ancient way. Northern people serve ice trays first at summer banquets, with fruit mixed in to eat. Poor people may just gnaw on ice instead of drinking, which easily leads to abdominal diseases. It's better to prohibit it.

Its sound is like a baby's. Eating it will drive you crazy.

Leaf fish have tails that branch out like leaves and patterns on their heads. They are found in the Philippines. Eel fish are very beautiful, several feet long, and winding like snakes. It is said that being bitten causes deafness. Lion fish, despite the name, are shaped like horses but without hooves. Zebra fish have zebra-like spots and delicious meat for cooking. Crab-foot fish have fins shaped like sticks, very much like crab feet, and are said to be very poisonous, capable of killing people. All are displayed in the Philippines' aquarium.

Black dolphins are beasts with fish tails and are found in the Pacific Ocean.

In the Japanese sea, there are fish that are no different from humans, but bald-headed and with tails, called sea monks.

Mud monkeys, also known as sea sharks, are round and long with round heads and protruding eyes. The gill covers have wart-like growths. Their backs are dark blue and their bellies are white. There are four black round spots on both sides. The tail is fan-shaped. They are two or three inches long and live in estuaries where fresh and saltwater mix. The gills can store water and the pectoral fins can crawl. They often crawl on the tidal sands and can jump on land as easily as monkeys, hence the name. They are also called mudskippers, which is the same name as gobies.

Oily fish, also known as weasel fish, are very flat and short, with wide heads that taper to the tail. The upper jaw is longer than the lower jaw. There are several pairs of whiskers next to the mouth. There are two pairs of whip-like bodies on the throat, transformed from the pelvic fins. The dorsal, anal, and caudal fins are connected. The body is covered with smooth, elliptical comb-like scales. The back is dark brown and the belly is blue. The eyes and scales are the color of weasels. They are eight or nine inches to one foot three or four inches long and are found in the Pacific Ocean, living in rocky areas near the coast.

Sailfish are up to thirteen or fourteen feet long and live in the open ocean. They like to swim in the upper layers of the water and often use their sword-like upper jaw to stab other fish or dig into the bottom of ships and sand. The meat is light red and tastes good. They are distributed in the Pacific Ocean and the Mediterranean Sea. The Atlantic Ocean also produces them. They are also called rudder fins or feather fish.

Electric light fish live along the coast of the United States. These fish can emit light at night, which is beneficial for navigation, no less than a lighthouse.

Publishing News: The Medical Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs, recognizing the rampant flames of the enemy and the urgent need for the people to be prepared with knowledge of defense against poisonous gases, has compiled and printed a book entitled "Essentials of Chemical Warfare." In addition to detailing the chemical properties of various poisonous gases, the methods of making poisonous gases, and the symptoms and treatments for victims of poisonous gases, the contents also focus on general protection methods and urban protection methods. The descriptions of the release of poisonous gases and aerial attacks are particularly realistic. Each volunteer team, each organization, each school, and people from all walks of life must have a copy in order to be prepared. The entire book is about 200 pages with more than ten illustrations. It is sold cheaply for six jiao, to promote widespread awareness (add seven jiao for postage).

Rotary Club of Storytellers

Sharing the Enemy (9)

— Gu Mingdao

Chapter Two: Like-Minded and United in Purpose

From then on, he also saw through Mei Guo's character and didn't like to waste words with him. Fortunately, Zhong Shu would come to chat from time to time and accompany him on outings nearby. Mei Guo had learned that Hua Naiqiang was a pauper and gradually became cold towards him. After two weeks, he couldn't bear it any longer. So, he said goodbye to Zhong Shu and returned to school first. Later, Zhong Shu came to the school, and the two of them talked about Zhong Shu's father in their spare time. Zhong Shu also admitted that her father was a warlord and that their views were not aligned. Hua Naiqiang said to Zhong Shu, "I am simply dissatisfied with your father's behavior. I don't listen to a word he says. Please don't be offended. I shouldn't be saying bad things about your father in front of you. The most embarrassing thing was that scene of beating the concubine the other day, which made me feel uneasy. If it weren't for your father, I would definitely..." Hua Naiqiang paused here and said, "Then again, those big shots who hold military power and sit high in the government are self-important and tyrannical. How many of them are clean and self-respecting, working for the country and the people? The world is full of them. It's not just your father." He sighed. Zhong Shu blushed and said, "Isn't that so? The way things are, how can China be good? Seeing my father's behavior makes me very ashamed. I have repeatedly advised him, but he refuses to listen and says I shouldn't meddle in his affairs." Hua Naiqiang said, "This is a matter of individual nature and cannot be generalized. It is rare to find someone like you, Madam, who is so insightful and patriotic." Zhong Shu smiled shyly again. From then on, Hua Naiqiang knew that Zhong Shu's father was such a person and felt sorry for her. It was also unfortunate to be born into such a powerful family. The day before the incident happened, the two of them were sitting on the grass in the west corner of the exercise field after practice, talking. The golden sunset shone on a large elm tree behind them. The cool breeze blew Zhong Shu's short hair around her ears. Zhong Shu rubbed her hands and said to Hua Naiqiang, "Our country's diplomacy is so slow. It has been so long since the Wanbaoshan Massacre, but there is still no solution. Is it true that weak countries have no diplomacy? Are our people just going to be slaughtered by others? The ignorant Koreans don't know the pain of losing their country and are willing to be used by others. They are both pitiful and hateful." Hua Naiqiang said, "This is the development of the Sun Country's Korean immigrant promotion and protection policy. They move Korean people to our country to open up land for them. When the time comes, they use them for military actions or large-scale conflicts, and then use the pretext of suppression to help them carry out their ambitions. They have coveted our borders for a long time. For decades, they have been doing it every day. I think this riot is just a test. There are more ruthless means to come."

Securities and Bond Prices Continue to Fall

Demobilization 20 Bonds Fall by $1.50

Other Small Amounts Vary from Several Cents to $1

However, the future of the bond market remains very chaotic, and the trend is still difficult to determine. The total spot transactions for the day amounted to $48,000, futures transactions amounted to over $2.2 million in the morning and $1.7 million in the afternoon, totaling $3.95 million.

American Cotton Showed No Improvement Last Week

A telegram from New York on the 11th reported on the cotton market for the week, stating that the government's estimated report on cotton harvest quantities on Tuesday did not increase significantly, being about 300,000 bales less than the public expected. This triggered short covering, but when prices rose by 0.10-0.15 pounds, there were fewer buyers, so the market soon turned loose. Grains and securities showed no improvement, and after the report, cotton prices were still disappointing, leading to more aggressive speculative selling at present, and old long positions were also being liquidated. There is still rain in the South, and the movement of new cotton is hindered, which may also lower the cotton quality, but some also believe it is beneficial to the soil. The hibernation of boll weevils is about 10% more than last year.
