Grain and Downstream Rice Market Suddenly Tightens

South Side: Yesterday, it was cold and windy, and there were few arrivals downstream. Shops in this street became active. Ordinary Northern Non-glutinous rice and Jiangsu Same White Non-glutinous rice suddenly increased by $0.20. There was a slight amount of Bo Dao Ning rice available, and sales were stable. There was not much refined Lu Yang rice available, and the price was high. Early rice was sold as soon as it arrived, with prices increasing significantly. There were not many sales of foreign rice to customers, and there were price cuts. Futures prices continued to be sold off by foreign firms, and the market was stable.

New Gate: Yesterday, the weather was not good, and there was a limited supply of Ordinary Xi Bai Non-glutinous rice. There was a slight amount of sporadic sales. The top and second grades showed no improvement. Shops purchased inventory. Wuxi and Kunshan rice each increased by $0.20. There was a lack of Chonggu and Songjiang Bo Dao rice arriving, and the situation tightened by $0.10. There was a limited supply of Yang Du refined rice arriving, and downstream areas and rice mills had a slight amount of inventory, also increasing by $0.20. Glutinous rice sales were flat, and the market had no ups or downs. Westbound rice boats, including Changshu, Kunshan, Danyang, and Jiaoli Beiban, numbered over thirty.

Foreign Rice Looks to Rise

Impact of Military Operations in Annam: Yesterday, the foreign rice market suddenly became active. Various foreign firms stopped selling, and brokers did not return to sell. It was reported that French troops were conducting military operations in Annam, and Saigon rice may be banned from export. Therefore, people hoped for improvement, and the market is expected to rise. However, there has been no action from customer groups, and there is still a large amount of fixed rice in various parts of Burma. Whether prices can rise is still uncertain. Spot rice from the Hankou group has stopped shipping. This street handled one shipment of Saigon rice for $11.20 per bag, and 500 bags of small-grain rice for $9.60 to $9.35 per bag.

Flour Falls Sharply, Then Slightly Rebounds

Yesterday, flour generally showed a sharp fall followed by a slight rebound. Foreign wheat quotations rebounded by about $0.02-0.03. In addition, after the large sell-off the day before, various factories were watching and waiting. Because factories must have foreign wheat orders placed before they are willing to sell, otherwise they will ignore any rises or falls, people's hearts have settled slightly, and the market has also rebounded by $0.01-0.02. However, if foreign wheat continues to be inquired about, the situation is still not optimistic. As a result, this month increased by $0.01 compared to the previous day, January increased by $0.01, February to April each increased by $0.0225, and May increased by $0.02.

Forward Wheat Rebounds

Yesterday, the forward wheat market showed signs of a general rise. Because this month is only one week away from delivery, off-market buying and selling must be settled. If flour sales are still good, factories still intend to collect this month's goods. However, the current situation offers little hope for the future, so the market atmosphere has not improved. Forward months all saw rebounds as foreign wheat was quoted higher and short covering was quite active. However, in general, this kind of rebound has little foundation. As a result, this month decreased by $0.01 compared to the previous day, January increased by $0.02, and February to April each increased by $0.06.

Local News

Li Jingcong Discusses Test Flights to Xinjiang

Today, Mr. Li Undertakes an Unprecedented Long-Distance Flight

Details Northwest Test Flight to Reporters

The Riri News Agency reports: Li Jingcong, an expert in pioneering aviation in remote areas, head of the Aviation Department of the Ministry of Transportation, and concurrently head of the Operations Section of Eurasia Aviation Corporation, successfully opened the air route from Beiping to Manchuria across the Hinggan Mountains in May of this year. It is now learned that he is scheduled to undertake a test flight to Xinjiang today (the 13th), which is an unprecedented initiative in Chinese aviation. Yesterday, a Riri News Agency reporter visited Mr. Li for a lengthy conversation, during which he provided a detailed account of the events before and after the Northwest test flight. The details are recorded below:

Reasons for the Test Flight: The Northwest route is one of the three major air routes planned by the Ministry of Transportation and the Qingcheng Corporation. Previously, the company believed that the public's understanding of aviation was still weak, making it difficult to develop aviation business. Furthermore, due to limited capital, it was difficult to prepare for this world's only long-distance route in a short period of time. Therefore, it was decided to postpone the endeavor for three to five years. However, the Party and government authorities, along with the general public, deeply felt that the situation between the inland and remote areas was too isolated, and the flow of information was too obstructed. This led to direct or indirect impacts on politics, culture, national defense, industry, and other aspects, resulting in a near-unanimous demand for immediate action. The company, unwilling to disregard the expectations of the entire nation, had no choice but to reluctantly undertake the task. Furthermore, due to being shot at by Mongolian soldiers while passing through Outer Mongolia in July and being obstructed by Japanese troops during a test flight to Taonan in September, the company decided to overcome the difficulties and first conduct the Northwest test flight. After its success, preparations for formally opening the route would be made based on the actual situation.

Route Selection: After the company decided to conduct the test flight, General Manager Shuang Qing sent Mr. Li and Mr. Schmidt to Beiping in October to make preparations. The most important aspect of the preparations was the route selection. Based on geographical and climatic factors, Mr. Li and his team originally planned to adopt a route of approximately 4,000 kilometers from Shanghai to Beijing, passing through Henan, Shaanxi, and Gansu directly into Xinjiang. According to investigations, although Henan Province has strong winds, it is a vast plain, making it easy to land in case of difficulties, minimizing the possibility of accidents. Shaanxi and Gansu, on the other hand, experience fewer drastic climate changes, and the mountains are not particularly high. Furthermore, the route passes through major cities with airfields or vast plains suitable for landing. However, due to the prevalence of bandits in Gansu Province, making it impossible to transport gasoline, this route could not be selected. Instead, the current route of approximately 4,200 kilometers from Shanghai to Beijing, then through Shandong, Hebei, Suiyuan, Ningxia, and directly into Xinjiang was adopted. Except for the smooth journey from Shanghai to Beiping, there are no difficulties on this route. However, the section from Beiping to Bailin Temple in Suiyuan requires traversing dense mountains. The section from Bailin Temple to Ruoshui River in Ningxia requires crossing vast wilderness. The same applies to the section from Ruoshui River to Hami in Xinjiang. Moreover, these areas frequently experience strong winds and severe cold weather. According to investigations, there are many places to land and the climate is good from Hami to Dihua, which is not as daunting and concerning as the sections between Bailin Temple and Ruoshui River, and Ruoshui River and Hami. On these two sections, straying from the designated route would lead to being lost in the boundless wilderness, with no signs of life and no water, posing a deadly threat to travelers. The designated route is also easily covered by sandstorms. If the aircraft encounters such a situation during the initial test flight, and the engine also malfunctions, it is difficult to imagine how rescue could be carried out. It is regrettable that the ideal and suitable route through the Shaanxi-Gansu heartland cannot be used due to the prevalence of bandits and the impossibility of transporting gasoline.

Gasoline Storage: Except for Bailin Temple, which is only over a hundred kilometers from Guihua, making gasoline transportation and storage relatively easy, the company hired a Swedish national familiar with the Ruoshui River area, Mr. Ruisenheng, at great expense. It took him over forty days to transport and store gasoline in the upper reaches of the Ruoshui River, a place suitable for aircraft landing and a ground landmark, located dozens of kilometers south of Juyanhai, also known as Youhe. Inland merchants traveling to Xinjiang typically travel in groups, employing Mongolians as guides. However, the Mongolian guides only know the direction to follow from one station to another and where to cross the Ruoshui River. They are unaware of the exact location of the crossing point on the Ruoshui River, the surrounding terrain, and whether it is suitable for aircraft landing. The opening of inland transportation requires seeking guidance from foreign lands, which is truly lamentable. Regarding the gasoline to be prepared in Xinjiang, the Ministry of Transportation has requested the Xinjiang Provincial Government to purchase Russian aircraft gasoline locally. Since Russia has already established two air routes to the Xinjiang border, with a significant amount of gasoline stored at the border, purchasing from them is faster and cheaper than transporting from the inland, saving up to three months of time.

Aircraft Improvements: The Northwest route, from Beiping to Hami, requires traversing approximately 2,000 kilometers of dense mountains and vast wilderness with obstructed transportation and sparse population. It is truly a long-distance route unique in the world and difficult to manage. Therefore, the selection of aircraft components should prioritize durability, suitability for long-distance travel, and a proven track record. The aircraft used by the company for the test flight meets the above requirements. It is a Junkers W33, serial number 33, all-metal fuselage, with a Junkers L5, 300-horsepower engine, a carrying capacity of 1,200 kilograms, a flight speed of 180 kilometers per hour, and an endurance of ten hours, or 1,800 kilometers. Special improvements and ample additions have been made to personnel cold protection, engine insulation, water filtration, fire prevention, and other equipment. Regarding personnel, before deciding to conduct the Northwest test flight, the company requested the Ministry of Transportation to inquire with the Xinjiang authorities about their opinions. They received a reply expressing their welcome and providing various reports related to aviation, such as ground and climate conditions.

The company also requested the Ministry of Transportation to telegraph the authorities of Suiyuan and Ningxia provinces, ordering military police and banner leaders along the route to provide full protection and assistance. Furthermore, General Manager Shuang Qing went north to Beiping to oversee everything. Beiping is the central hub of the entire Shanghai-Xinjiang line, making it the most convenient location to handle any unexpected technical or personnel issues. Therefore, the company does not anticipate difficulties with these preparations, especially in terms of personnel. Publicity and Mail Delivery: In addition to submitting a request to the National Government through the Ministry of Transportation and consulting relevant authorities to have various official documents recently sent to Xinjiang delivered by the company, the company also sent a letter to the Directorate General of Posts, instructing the Shanghai and Beiping postal administrations to package five kilograms of recently mailed letters to Xinjiang separately and hand them over to the company for postal flight testing. Separate letters were sent to major newspapers in Shanghai and Beiping, requesting them to package ten copies of the day's news each and hand them over to the company for promotional purposes. Furthermore, the company and the China Weekly News Agency reprinted various printed materials to be distributed in the air upon arrival in Dihua to increase the Northwest public's understanding of aviation.

Flight Time and Location: Mr. Li is scheduled to lead Eurasia No. 3 to Beiping today (Sunday, the 13th). After resting in Beiping for one day, he will switch to Eurasia No. 1 at 8:00 a.m. on the 15th and fly to Bailin Temple, a distance of over 520 kilometers, arriving at 10:55 a.m. After arriving, about half a day will be needed for arrangements. At 8:00 a.m. on the 16th, he will fly to Ruoshui River, a distance of over 780 kilometers from Bailin Temple, arriving at 12:20 p.m. After arriving, about half a day will be needed for arrangements. At 8:00 a.m. on the 17th, he will fly to Hami, a distance of over 660 kilometers from Ruoshui River, arriving at 11:40 a.m. After arriving, about half a day will be needed for arrangements. At 8:00 a.m. on the 18th, he will fly to Dihua, a distance of only over 460 kilometers, arriving at 10:35 a.m. Approximately at least one week will be needed in Dihua for arrangements and negotiations. At 8:00 a.m. on the 25th, he will fly to Tacheng, a distance of over 500 kilometers from Dihua, arriving at 10:50 a.m. After arriving, arrangements and negotiations will take about one and a half days. At 7:00 a.m. on the 27th, he should be able to fly back to Dihua. Whether he flies back to Beiping from Dihua in one go or in multiple stages will depend on the situation at that time. In any case, barring weather or other obstacles, he will definitely return to Shanghai within the year to report to the head office. Future Plans: After the success of this test flight, the first step will be to purchase equipment, recruit personnel, open airfields, build hangars, store gasoline, install wireless communication equipment, and establish necessary facilities for weather observation, emergency rescue, and sanitation. All of these will take at least three to four months. If there are no other obstacles in the meantime, the route can be officially opened by the end of April or the beginning of May next year. The second step will be to negotiate with Russia for joint operations in the Sino-Russian border area in Xinjiang. Eurasian postal flights cannot save much time and money unless they pass through Russia or engage in joint operations with Russia, which is too far from the original purpose of rapid air delivery. Passing through Russia is not currently feasible because Sino-Russian diplomatic relations have not been restored, but the Russian side has already approved the joint operation in Manchuria. Since this section has already been approved, it is expected that there will be no questions raised in the future about changing to joint operations in the Sino-Russian border area in Xinjiang. Furthermore, it takes six days to travel from Manchuria to Europe via Russia, compared to only five days from Xinjiang, saving one day in terms of time. This is not only what the people of Eurasia hope for, but Russia will also be more than willing to assist in this beneficial global undertaking. The third step is to reduce the flight time between Shanghai and Xinjiang. The air route from Shanghai to Xinjiang is over 4,200 kilometers long, and the flight time is approximately 24 hours. Except in summer, when it is possible to barely complete the flight in two days, it cannot be completed in less than three days in winter. To reduce the flight time, nighttime flight equipment is necessary. The most suitable section for nighttime flight equipment on this entire route is the Shanghai-Beiping section, and the section that best meets the principles of time and economic efficiency is the Bailin Temple-Hami section. However, since the Bailin Temple-Hami section passes through wilderness and often experiences strong winds, it is not easy to implement in the short term. Currently, only the Shanghai-Beiping section can be implemented. With successful implementation of the Shanghai-Beiping section, the journey from Shanghai to Xinjiang in winter will take two days and one night, while in summer it will only take one day and one night. In conclusion, the success of this route is of great importance both domestically and internationally. Mr. Li is extremely hopeful that this trip will be worthwhile.

A Visit with Mayor Zhang

A reporter from the Central News Agency visited Mayor Zhang yesterday evening to inquire about everything. Mayor Zhang answered each question in detail. A brief record is as follows: (Question) We heard that the Mayor's health is not well, so we came to inquire. How have you been recently? (Answer) My physical condition is still strong, but since the Northeast foreign invasion and the frequent international disputes in Shanghai, I have been focusing on these matters for the past three months, and I feel mentally and physically exhausted. Unexpectedly, a student protest suddenly erupted the other day. Although I tried my best to endure and bear the burden to quell the incident and appease the people, I could not sleep afterwards and felt brain swelling and headaches. I still feel unwell now. (Question) We heard that the Mayor planned to make an announcement to the newspapers the other day. Why has it not been published yet? (Answer) That is true, but the Central Government has ordered Commander Chen to investigate this case. As a rule, no public statements should be made during the investigation. However, I have prepared a detailed report of the incident and sent it to Commander Chen for an impartial investigation. It will be announced in due course. (Question) Are the news reports about the case and the Mayor's comments in the newspapers in recent days accurate? (Answer) There are some discrepancies, which I believe are due to errors in the rumors. (Question) The Central Government has sent a telegram to persuade you to stay. Can the Mayor's resignation be withdrawn? (Answer) I am determined to resign and have telegraphed again to request my resignation. If I am not allowed to resign, I will go to Beijing to insist on my resignation.

Chen Mingshu Announces His Views on Investigating the Shanghai Incident

Chen Mingshu, the Commander of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison, made the following comments to a Central News Agency reporter after receiving an order from the National Government to thoroughly investigate the student protest in Shanghai: I have come to Shanghai on the orders of the Central Government to investigate the unfortunate incident that occurred in Shanghai. I will conduct an impartial and thorough investigation to clarify the truth and report it to the Central Government for review and handling. During this investigation, I sincerely hope that all parties will remain calm, respect local order, and avoid creating further disputes, which would weaken the nation's united strength against foreign aggression. I believe that the Central Government will also handle this case impartially to satisfy public opinion. Chen went to Beijing last night.

Student Representatives from Various Universities Paid a Visit to Commander Chen Yesterday

Chen said that students should contribute opinions within the proper framework

And form a united force against foreign aggression with the government

And not forget the original intention of the student national salvation movement

Shen Zuru, Liu Ping, Lin Zumo, Wang Lizhong, Guan Zhaohui, Sheng Yuhua, Xiong Daji, and other representatives from the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Union of Shanghai Universities visited Commander Chen Mingshu of the Beijing-Shanghai Garrison at 6:00 p.m. yesterday to report on the Shanghai student protests on the 9th. After the representatives finished speaking, Chen expressed his views on the investigation of the student protests, saying: The course of the student protests has been investigated clearly, and I will be responsible for reporting the truth to the Central Government for disposition. As for the student national salvation movement, it arises from the purest and noblest enthusiasm. The government should sincerely accept this kind of well-intentioned petition, try its best to prevent military police from having misunderstandings and conflicts with the masses, and at the same time try its best to make the masses understand the government's diplomatic policy. The current organization of the Central National Crisis Conference and Mr. Wang's proposal for a national salvation conference are attempts to allow the public to participate in diplomacy. As for whether to advocate for war or peace, it cannot be decided with one word. The government is willing to share the responsibility with the public. As for the students, they should also contribute opinions to the government within the proper framework and serve as the government's backing. Going beyond the framework is not the way for the government and the people to unite against foreign aggression. In short, I hope that all of you students will cooperate with the government in the future to form a united force against foreign aggression and awaken the masses to unleash the great national strength to save ourselves. Do not be incited by the illegal and excessive slogans of reactionary elements, so that the results will be that what was initiated for the country and the nation becomes an action that harms the country and the nation. Therefore, I especially hope that students will pay close attention and never forget the original intention of the student mass national salvation movement. After Chen's remarks, the student representatives expressed their satisfaction and returned. (New Voice News Agency)

Anti-Japanese Association of University Professors Hosts Reporters

The Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of University Professors in Shanghai hosted a tea party for reporters from various newspapers at the China News Agency on Weihaiwei Road at 3:00 p.m. yesterday to report on the purpose of the association's organization and the attitude it holds. First, Jin Tongyin, a professor at Fudan University, delivered a speech, stating that the purpose of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Association of University Professors in Shanghai is to cooperate in academic research, guide young people with enthusiasm, and critique facts from a detached position. Then, Zhang Yi explained the association's attitude. The full text is as follows: "I have been entrusted by the board of directors of our association to briefly explain our association's attitude to everyone. The details are as follows: (1) Regarding the Northeast Incident, our association believes that armed resistance must be implemented, safeguarding the territory while recovering lost land. There are four reasons for this: (A) Driven by facts, Japan's aggression is endless. Since the fall of the three provinces, it has continued to attack Jinzhou, disrupt Tianjin, and threaten Shanghai and Wuhan, gradually invading the hinterland. Without resistance, the country will inevitably perish. (B) Promoting unity. If those in power can truly rise up to defend the country, it will not be difficult to restore public trust, and internal unity will not be a problem. (C) Coercing the powers. If the war expands and endangers the East Asian market, the powers will inevitably make more impartial demands based on their interests. Simply wagging our tails and begging them will only result in perfunctory treatment. (D) Maintaining national dignity. If the country is humiliated to this extent and still swallows its anger and endures humiliation, it will be unworthy of survival in the world. The public should have long known that the League of Nations is unreliable. The recent resolution clearly favors Japan, and the investigation team is particularly unfavorable to our country. Our association firmly opposes it. (2) Regarding the attitude towards the government, our association observes the government and believes that it is (A) not clean,

Page 18

(B) without a direction, (C) without ability. Such a government is already difficult to handle in peacetime. Today, with the national crisis at hand, we know that it will cause great harm. However, since it is actually exercising its powers, our association believes that it must be subject to strict supervision by the people. Recently, the government has always asked the people to trust it. In fact, the people have always longed for a trustworthy government. In the past four years, the people have never interfered in politics, which can be said to be the utmost trust, but the result has become the current situation. "To this day, they still do not know how to repent," and they empty words of being determined to resist foreign aggression. They have made no military preparations, are unwilling to be open in diplomacy, only know to trust the League of Nations, and internally, there is no hope of unity. They do not know how to properly guide the spontaneous patriotism of students, but instead falsely accuse them of being incited by others. How can such actions make the people trust them? "Therefore, our association insists on the necessity of supervision. As for the national crisis conference that the government is preparing, it must be an organ that can truly represent public opinion in order to be accepted by the public. If the government arbitrarily appoints a number of people who are obedient to the government's wishes to cover up the eyes and ears of the people, then the crime will be more unforgivable than simply ignoring the people's wishes." (3) Regarding the attitude towards the party headquarters, the responsibility of the party headquarters, according to themselves, is to supervise the government and guide the people, but in fact, diplomacy has failed to such an extent, what can the party headquarters do? The government is produced by the party, and what supervision does the party give it? Moreover, at this critical moment, they are still splitting and quarreling, determined to plunge the country into eternal ruin. They are not making efforts for the anti-Japanese national salvation work, can they guide the people? In the past, we have only seen them suppressing speech, interfering with meetings, and detaining news. For those who disagree with them, they often add the title of "reactionary" to vent personal grudges. The lives of the country and the nation have long been out of their minds. Recently, incidents of kidnapping students have actually occurred in this city, which is truly unbearable to speak of." It is found that the party headquarters is not an administrative agency, and in the future, its powers should be strictly limited, its personnel should be strictly screened, and its speech and actions should be subject to legal sanctions just like the people. (4) Regarding the student movement, since 1927, the spirit of the May Fourth Movement has been lost. Under high pressure, the students appear to be disciplined, but in fact their core has long been decadent. There are three main symptoms: (A) living frivolously, (B) unwilling to study diligently, and (C) currying favor with officials to engage in personal political activities. It can be said that they have been numb for a long time. This time, driven by their conscience, they have shown patriotism and swept away the accumulated malpractices over the years, which can be said to be commendable. This movement has made great contributions to the country, and it is also a transformative turning point for the students themselves. The future of the country depends on the youth. It is necessary to have young people with strong will, clear minds, and rich emotions to create a brand new country. Therefore, we hope that the anti-Japanese national salvation movement can be expanded into the New Youth Movement, which is the fundamental plan for saving the country. This admirable and valuable vigorous vitality of the New Youth is also the vitality of the Chinese nation. Our association is willing to support it wholeheartedly. In short, our association recognizes its own position and mission, and its attitude is not willing to be brutal, but it is extremely firm. It not only has firm views, but will also take action when necessary. We are honored by your presence today, and we hope that you will give us your guidance."

Then, Xie Xunchu reported on the association's work, stating that the association was established on November 27th and has only been two weeks since, so there are no achievements to speak of. As for the work, it is divided into three departments: research, translation, and propaganda. Finally, Fan Jingwu represented the guests and gave a speech, hoping that the association would be permanently established and strive forward.

Wang Jingwei Delivers an Important Speech Yesterday

The National Salvation Conference is Different from the National Crisis Conference

The Powers and Limits of the Party Headquarters and Government Agencies Must Be Delineated

Mr. Wang Jingwei, a representative from Guangdong, gave the following speech to reporters from various news agencies yesterday: Reporter (Question) Are the National Salvation Conference advocated by Mr. Wang and the National Crisis Conference the same in name and substance? Wang (Answer) The important constituent members of the National Salvation Conference I advocate are representatives of people's organizations. This is the difference between the National Salvation Conference and the National Crisis Conference. (Question) Are celebrities and scholars required to join? (Answer) Of course, they are welcome, but the important constituent members must be representatives of people's organizations. Only in this way can the foundation of democratic politics be established. (Question) Is this conference a temporary conference specifically set up to deal with the national crisis? (Answer) In order to deal with the national crisis, there should be this conference. Even if the national crisis is over, there only needs to be an organ representing public opinion in peacetime. (Question) Are the candidates for this organ representing public opinion limited to members of the Chinese Nationalist Party? (Answer) Of course, they are not limited to members of the Chinese Nationalist Party. (Question) If so, does it conflict with party rule? (Answer) To answer this question, please review my essays "How to Establish Democratic Forces" published on November 3, 1929, and "How to Realize Democratic Politics" published on October 20, 1929. You should know that for several years, I have consistently advocated that the people's rights in the tutelage era should increase day by day in time and expand day by day in space. Only in this way can the purpose of tutelage be achieved, and only then can we transition from tutelage to constitutionalism. (Question) In Mr. Wang's opinion, what should be the relationship between the party headquarters and the people? (Answer) To answer this question, please review my essay "The Meaning of Party Rule" published on January 11, 1930. The main points are as follows: (1) Since we have determined that the party is within the people, our advocacy is not only for the above-mentioned organs of public opinion (whether it is the permanent National Assembly or the temporary National Conference, or even the small affairs of the conference organs in cities, towns, and villages), but also for various people's organizations, such as commercial groups, labor groups, peasant groups, etc., we should respect their independence. The party can only use various efforts to make them automatically accept the leadership of the party, and should never oppress them. (2) Not only is this the case for the above-mentioned organs of public opinion and people's organizations, but also the relationship between the party headquarters and government agencies must be clearly delineated. The party should guide and supervise comrades working in government agencies according to the party's ideology and policies to ensure that they are implemented. It should not directly replace government agencies and issue orders externally. (3) We advocate that the judiciary should be completely independent. (4) We advocate that there should be clear regulations on the freedom of assembly, publication, and speech of the people. The party's propositions and fundamental policies must not be violated, but in their implementation, the people outside the party should not only be allowed to participate in opinions, but also be allowed to participate in actions, and even be allowed to criticize and supervise. (Question) Does Mr. Wang still insist on this proposition now? (Answer) For several years, I and my colleagues who worked together for this proposition have been displaced and suffered hardships, and have remained unswerving. How can there be no reason to insist on it? We regard the proposition as ten times more important than the people's problems. Now, let me tell you in advance that if I and my colleagues are allowed to enter Nanjing, and this proposition cannot be implemented, then we will have no choice but to resolutely abandon it. No matter who is in power, we will hold this attitude. Furthermore, if anyone among me and my colleagues abandons this proposition, then that person will no longer be a comrade in whom we trust, and we will do our best to oppose him.

The National Government Denies the Secret Order to Arrest Major University Presidents

Official Statement from the Secretariat Yesterday

Yesterday, a letter from Zheng Hongnian and others was published in the newspapers. The Secretariat of the National Government issued a statement, stating that the content of the letter was not factual. The statement reads: "We have seen the letter from Zheng Hongnian, Li Zhaohuan, He Shizhen, and Chen Qun published in the Shanghai newspapers, which is quite shocking. The National Government has always been tolerant of the patriotic movements of various schools, which is a well-known fact. There has never been any order to arrest the principals of the schools whose names are on the letter. It is difficult to guess whether this letter was written according to the wishes of the signatories, but the National Government has never issued the secret order mentioned in the letter, which should be corrected. The Secretariat of the National Government."

Telegram from the Foreign Advisor to Mayor Zhang

Shi Zhaoji Clarifies Rumors Reported in Newspapers

Special Foreign Affairs Committee Telegraphed Asking Him to Withdraw His Resignation

The Foreign Advisor telegraphed Shanghai Mayor Zhang: "I have just received a telegram from Representative Shi stating that a certain newspaper in Paris reported yesterday that I had vaguely suggested to Dawes that Chinese troops could withdraw to Jinzhou. I met with Dawes on the morning of the 10th of this month. Dawes planned to make a statement on the Jinzhou issue that afternoon. I told him that China had no proposals to make on this issue and that we absolutely could not consider the neutral zone and the withdrawal of troops from Jinzhou. Dawes stated that he did not know about the report in the newspaper, which was clearly a rumor. I am telegraphing to clarify." Recently, there have been many misunderstandings in foreign news. Please inform the members of the Second, Fourth, and Sixth Committees of the above matters to clarify the truth. The Special Foreign Affairs Committee telegraphed Shanghai Mayor Zhang Qun: "Upon receiving your telegram, we were all surprised and worried. The students' actions are excessive, mostly due to a lack of experience and a lack of central leadership. Now that the League of Nations has made a resolution and our rights have been declared and reserved, all patriotic citizens with opinions have heard and seen them. In the future, the whole country will be united and the goal of resisting foreign aggression will not be difficult to achieve. All rumors will soon disappear. Shanghai's relationship is of great importance. The government and the people are grateful for your hard work in maintaining it. We earnestly hope that you will withdraw your resignation and work hard for the country. Right and wrong will be judged fairly."

Declaration by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce

The Government Must Adopt an Open and Inclusive Attitude

The People Must Not Harbor Suspicion or Speculation

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce held a joint meeting of directors and supervisors yesterday afternoon at 4 PM. Wang Xiaolai, Wang Yansong, Xu Jiqing, Yuan Ludeng, Fang Jiaobo, Bei Songsun, Pei Yunqing, Zhu Wenqi, Lu Fengzhu, Luo Qinghua, Wu Zhihao, Lu Qisheng, Wen Lanting, Ma Jiyi, Cheng Xiechun, Jiang Zhigang, Lao Jingxiu, and over twenty others attended. Wang Xiaolai chaired the meeting. After a long discussion, it was decided to issue the following declaration: "Since the Japanese forcibly occupied the Three Eastern Provinces, what the people expect from the government under the current circumstances is: first, to strengthen preparations for self-defense, so that when Japanese violence comes, there will not be a situation of being caught unprepared and defeated; second, to exercise the rights of a member state of the League of Nations, and to seek the realization of all the provisions stipulated in the covenant, and not to allow the League of Nations to be timid and evasive and avoid responsibility. These two major reasons are the only way to deal with violent Japan. No matter how difficult and tortuous, the government has an unshirkable responsibility to fulfill its mission of saving the country and protecting the people. However, in the past two months, the government's actions and the facts that have been revealed to the people have not been consistent with these two major principles. In terms of self-defense, it has been trying to avoid confrontation and has been making concessions and retreats, and has not been able to show that it has the strength to protect the land and secure the people. In terms of diplomacy, the League of Nations has become more and more soft, and our country's attitude has also become more and more accommodating. When the people are heartbroken by the foreign troubles, they are stirred up with indignation and turned into disappointment, which is also a constant human emotion. However, we believe that the people should make suggestions to the government in peacetime, and should not harbor suspicion or speculation. As for when the country is in a very unusual event and the people's hearts are shaken with apprehension, they should especially abide by the poet's so-called "diligently turn to the heart, and should not have anger." All the government's facilities, such as failure to meet the will of the Prime Minister, the country and hope, should be dripping and said, phase in the ancient saying of "sincerity is the key, gold and stone is the key" purpose, and for the government, should also hold the empty has the capacity of attitude, the ancient people's hearing of the wrong is happy, see good is worship, can turn indignation into peace, if each other fire and water, mutual discrimination, then the boat enemy, moderate plan to find those who alienate the psychology, foreign force violent enemy, internal affairs strife, how can there be any reason to fortunately complete. Our Association, in its position as the leader of the city's business people, when the country is in trouble, if it is helpful to the country, then since the economic severance of relations with Japan, the capital stranded by businessmen, as well as the direct and indirect effects, although in Shanghai is an unprecedented record, it should also be喻以大义, so that it can try to endure, on the one hand, to promote domestic goods, actively produce, consolidate finance, stabilize the business market, and plant the foundation for national salvation. If you start to disturb each other, rashly stop working, and do not damage the enemy's haom, it is just enough to destroy the lifeblood of the country, then you dare not blindly follow, to tự貽复亡 of the misfortune. All in all, the work of saving the country is only in doing our best, and helping each other in the same boat. We hope that all gentlemen from all walks of life in the city will understand this together."

Declaration by the Two Postal Workers' Unions

The Shanghai Postal Workers' Union and the Postal Employees' Union held an emergency joint meeting the other day, and issued a solemn declaration regarding the incident of the Student Federation, stating: "To all organizations and newspaper offices, and to our fellow compatriots across the country: Since the Kuomintang has been in power, all the measures taken have been limited by the difficulties of the times, and those that can satisfy the people's aspirations have been very few. As of today, an unprecedented flood and the Shenyang Incident have forced the authorities to take the blame for negligence and to fulfill their responsibility to remedy the situation. At this time of crisis, the people, seeing that there is no time to save the dying, how can they bear to blame them for their faults? They should also understand the difficulty of dealing with the situation, which the authorities cannot bear alone. Therefore, on the one hand, they have risen up to organize and urge the authorities, and on the other hand, they are rushing to risk their lives to help the victims, hoping to save the country from danger in an instant, and to fulfill their duty as citizens. Their hearts are extremely bitter, and their situation is extremely miserable. However, up until now, the peace and defense that the people have been striving for have not been realized. The international situation is deteriorating, and the Japanese invaders are attacking more and more urgently. The people are crying and begging, but they have not heard that the authorities have given them any consideration. At this time, the people, driven by righteousness, have risen up to carry out the national salvation movement. Even if there are occasional extreme situations, it is a direct expression of the people's legitimate demands and an indirect symbol of the authorities' failure to fulfill their responsibilities. The authorities cannot guide them to the right path, but only use obstruction as a strategy. If this continues, when will the disputes end? This Association, in view of the difficulties of the times, specially convened an emergency joint meeting on the 11th, and all agreed that the incident of the Student Federation was the result of the authorities' inability to guide the patriotic movement of the people, and indirectly was caused by the failure to achieve peaceful unification within the country. The way to get to the root of the problem is that, on the part of the authorities, both the Ning and Yue sides should abide by the resolutions of the peace talks, with Commander-in-Chief Jiang of the Ning side going north to recover the lost territory on an appointed date, and the members of the Yue side immediately going to Beijing to jointly bear the responsibility of the country, establish a unified government, and revive the national revolution. On the part of the people, they should all be based on the spirit of patriotism, improve their organizations, unify their steps, concentrate their strength, and support each other. When necessary, they can organize a joint meeting of people's organizations to connect with the government authorities and achieve the effect of mutual support. Regarding this incident, the authorities should make a positive determination to properly handle the aftermath so that this dispute can be peacefully resolved. Saving the Party and saving the country depend on this. This Association and others are not behind anyone in their love of country and revolution. All propositions concerning national affairs have been communicated and declared in the past, and we will continue to seek their implementation in the spirit of revolution. We hereby declare this, and we hope that you will all understand."

Local News Two

Record of the Interrogation of Hong Weiji

Arrested and Searched at Hong's Residence Due to Report from Chinese Authorities

Defendant Released on Bail by Shen Junru

Sentencing Scheduled for the 15th

Hong Weiji, also known as Wei Ji, a 30-year-old student at the Shanghai Art College and chairman of the Anti-Japanese Association, who previously served as a people's court judge in the Shanghai Municipal Government, was arrested by the French police on suspicion of being a communist. He was later released on bail by the secretary of the Municipal Government. Yesterday morning, he was summoned by the police to the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court for questioning. A large number of people were present to observe the proceedings, including classmates from the Art College and students from other schools, creating a crowded scene. At 10 AM, acting presiding judge Guo Dechang, along with judges Zhang Chaozuo and Li Changnian, prosecutor Zhang Zongkan, and clerk Liu Zongyi, took their seats in the first courtroom for the hearing. First, Gu Shouxi, the police lawyer, presented the case, stating that the arrest was based on a report from the Chinese authorities that the defendant was suspected of being a communist, but the details were unclear. The defendant, Hong Weiji, stated that he found it strange that the police lawyer said the case was unclear. He asked how he could be arrested if the details were unknown. On the night of his arrest, he had been working as a people's judge during the day and was sleeping at home (upstairs at No. 16 Wende Lane, Beile Road). Police detectives knocked on the door and entered, but his door was unlocked, so the detectives went straight into the bedroom and arrested him. The detectives found a paper package on the table, which they claimed was communist evidence. Hong said that the paper package was sealed and he did not know where it came from. The detectives searched the drawers and other places and confiscated writings by students and anti-Japanese leaflets from the Datong Bookstore, but nothing else. He was taken to the Songshan Road Police Station. The next morning, he was sent to the General Police Station. The detectives asked him if he was a communist, which he denied. They then began to beat him, causing him to bleed, as evidenced by a medical certificate. The official asked if he had admitted at the police station that the communist leaflets were given to him by his friend Zhang Jie. Hong replied that he had. The police had told him to say that. Although Zhang was his classmate, the leaflets were not given to him by Zhang. He was asked if Zhang Jie had asked him to join the Communist Party when he gave him the leaflets. He said that he had not joined. The official asked if this was true. Hong replied that this was also what the detectives told him to say. He was also asked if Zhang Jie was a communist, to which he replied that he did not know. He was asked if he had heard Zhang Jie mention joining the Communist Party, to which he replied that he had not. The official asked the police lawyer who had motivated Hong's arrest. Lawyer Gu replied that it was the Chinese authorities. The lawyer had not inquired in detail due to the short time he had to attend court. He requested that the presiding judge question the Western detective who was handling the case for more details. The official ordered the Western detective to appear. The detective stated that the police had received a report from the Chinese authorities and went to the defendant's home to search. They found a paper package on the table, which contained communist leaflets. When asked, Hong stated that the leaflets were given to him by his friend Zhang Jie, and he intended to distribute them on the 11th. Hong Weiji stated that the detective's report was not consistent with the facts. The official asked the police lawyer if the police had any concrete evidence to prove that Hong was a communist. Lawyer Gu then asked the Western detective in French and replied that the Western detective said that in June of this year, regarding the Annam communist incident, the defendant had reported it. The official asked the defendant if it was true that he had reported it. Lawyer Gu asked the Western detective again, who replied that the police could not remember whether the defendant had come to report it, but they knew that the defendant often associated with the Annam communists. The official asked Hong Weiji if it was true, and Hong replied that it was not true at all. The police lawyer stated that to know the details, it would be necessary to request a postponement. At this point, the defendant's defense lawyers objected to the postponement. Prosecutor Zhang stated that all the evidence was already on file and requested that the debate begin. Presiding Judge Guo then ordered the debate to begin. First, the police lawyer argued that the police were only acting on a report from the Chinese authorities, alleging that the defendant was suspected of being a communist and endangering the Republic of China. The police arrested him because it was related to the security of the concession, and there were no other special circumstances. Next, the defendant's lawyers, Shen Junru and Zhang Runmin, argued that there was no evidence whatsoever to support the police's accusation that the defendant was a communist. If the defendant had communist activities, they would naturally be very secret, so why would he leave the door unlocked while sleeping and place communist leaflets on the table? The defendant, Hong Weiji, is the chairman of the Anti-Japanese Association and served as a people's judge before. That is why he was noticed. Furthermore, the incident of the student being abducted occurred on the 9th. The defense lawyers certified that the defendant's attitude was frank. This case occurred entirely after the defendant left the people's court, which shows that he was framed. They requested that he be declared innocent. Presiding Judge Guo declared the debate closed and announced that the sentencing would be held at 2 PM on the 15th. The defendant was ordered to be released on bail and appear whenever summoned. He was then released on bail by his lawyer, Shen Junru.

German Conspires with American to Steal Large Quantities of Relief Wheat

Selling the Wheat for Profit

Fortunately, the Crime Was Discovered and Arrests Made

This autumn, floods spread across various provinces, with Jiangsu, Hankou, and northern Jiangsu being the worst affected. People were displaced, and the dead were lying everywhere. The government and the United States purchased a large quantity of wheat for disaster relief in China. Several shipments have already been delivered to Shanghai and distributed to starving victims, as reported in the newspapers. A certain ship recently arrived in Shanghai with a large quantity of wheat, which was then unloaded onto a barge hired from the China Transportation Company at No. 24 Huangpu Bund Road. 946 bags of wheat worth 6,000 yuan were loaded onto the barge, which was docked in the river at the Yangshupu Lan Road wharf, for transportation to Hankou and northern Jiangsu to provide relief to starving victims. A German named Pian Tuo conspired with an American named Xie Gai, residing at No. 8 Yuanmingyuan Road, to remove all the wheat from the barge and transport it by car to a house at No. 23 Fude Road for storage, intending to secretly sell it for profit. However, a German named Tai Si discovered the plot and secretly reported it to the Hongkou Police Station. Western Detective Chief Nai Tieshan and others arrested Xie Gai and Pian Tuo one after another. Xie Gai was sent to the American Consulate for trial. The police also went to No. 23 Fude Road, recovered the stolen wheat, and brought it to the police station. Yesterday morning, Pian Tuo was sent to the First Special Court, Higher Court I. The police lawyer, Zhang Tianyin, stated the case and said that they were waiting for Xie Gai's interrogation by the American Consulate to verify the testimony of the defendant, so they requested a postponement. Western Detective Chief Nai Tie also stated that because Xie Gai owed him money, he said that this kind of wheat was bought by the United States and mortgaged to him. I didn't know that it was for disaster relief. After hearing his explanation, Judge Shen Bingrong ordered him to be detained and rescheduled the trial. The stolen goods were first handed over to the owner to take away.

Min Ti Ni Junction Uses Automatic Telephones

Telephone Company's Complete Plan

Two-Thirds Already Realized

The Shanghai Telephone Company is constructing the Min Ti Ni Junction at No. 106 Baliqiao Road in the French Concession, and is retrofitting with automatic telephones.

Exterior of the Min-ti-ni Exchange

Since construction began last August, it has been completed today. Telephones in the area will be switched to automatic operation today. The new three-story building is temporarily equipped with 6,000 pairs of lines, and can be expanded to 10,000 pairs in the future. If business develops, another machine can be added, laying 10,000 pairs of lines. Because the number of residents in the French Concession is increasing day by day, more room has been left for future development. Since last August, the company has successively built new exchanges and renovated automatic telephones. Five areas have now been completed, namely the central exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "1," the Huishan exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "5," the Bi-xun exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "7," the Min-ti-ni exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "8," and the Fujian exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "9." There are still three remaining manual exchanges, namely the Route des Soeurs exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "2," the western exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "3," and the northern exchange, where telephone numbers begin with "4." It is now estimated that two-thirds of the company's telephones have been converted to automatic telephones, and all telephones in the French Concession have been converted to automatic telephones since the completion of the Min-ti-ni exchange today.

Telegram from Veteran Party Member You Lie

A telegram from You Lie, a veteran member of the Nationalist Party, reads (titles omitted): "To the esteemed public, since the recovery of Xinhai, twenty years have passed in an instant. Internal strife has been incessant, disasters have been frequent, the people have been impoverished, and national defense has been lax, leading to foreign enemies taking advantage of the situation and strong neighbors seizing opportunities for aggression. Now the Japanese invaders' conspiracies have been exposed, and their ferocious flames are raging. The League of Nations' justice is not upheld, and the effectiveness of the agreements has been lost. In this period, crises are lurking everywhere, and dangers are pervasive. Our country has fallen into a state of nine deaths and one life, where advancement and retreat are both fraught with peril. As an old and mediocre man, I have endured much hardship. I do not wish to comment on national affairs, but seeing that the national pulse is about to be severed and the nation is on the verge of extinction, I am alarmed and vigilant, and I cannot help but speak out. At this critical and urgent time of life and death, all those with blood and spirit, regardless of whether they are in or out of office, or which party or faction they belong to, should eliminate prejudices, unite sincerely, concentrate all efforts, realize consistent demands, and avoid clinging to rigid demands, lest they cause further disputes. Do not take advantage of the situation or resort to trickery to achieve selfish desires. If we can gather the wise men of the country, unleash the true will of the people, reform and start anew, and strive for strength, we can work together with one heart and confront foreign enemies, then we can uphold justice, establish a diplomatic policy, and actively plan and prepare for armed resistance. Moreover, with the firm and激昂spirit of the people as a backing, we will surely be able to uphold justice, and with a powerful army that is just and righteous, we will be able to kill the enemy. What difficulty is there in destroying them as easily as eating breakfast? What is valuable is careful consideration and planning, fulfilling responsibilities and guarding boundaries, acting in a consistent order, and supporting each other, so that victory can be assured and mistakes can be avoided. Although I am old, I am willing to lead loyal comrades at home and abroad to prepare and await orders, ready to serve as a vanguard and face the national crisis together. This statement is urgent and I will never waver from my determination to die. I hope you will consider this. You Lie bows. Text and telegram to be sent from No. 114 North Sichuan Road, An Shen Fang Kou, 2nd floor, Shanghai."

Measures for the Ministry of Finance to Transport Cash for Export

The Banking Association decided to comply

The Shanghai Banking Association, after receiving the regulations on transporting silver for export stipulated by the Ministry of Finance a few days ago, submitted them for discussion at the standing committee meeting yesterday. They unanimously expressed their approval for the Ministry of Finance's measures to prevent unscrupulous merchants from seeking private gain and to avoid causing financial panic in the locality. They also agreed that the association should strictly investigate the transport of silver for export in the future to maintain the market. It was immediately decided to notify all members of the association in this city that anyone who transports silver for export must first contact the Banking Association, and then the association will notify the customs to ship it. At the same time, the regulations stipulated by the Ministry of Finance will also be copied and forwarded to the Banking Associations of Tianjin, Pingjin, and Hankou to achieve consistency. After the meeting, the two resolutions were sent to the respective parties.

Death of Ms. Zhu Hu Binxia

Ms. Zhu Hu Binxia, wife of Mr. Zhu Tiren, Director of the Salt Affairs Inspection Office, contracted typhoid fever last summer and has been recurring ever since. This summer, she went to Guling for recuperation. She gradually improved after her husband's death in Shanghai in the autumn. However, she caught a cold last Sunday, which developed into streptococcal meningitis. After being sent to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment, unfortunately, the bacteria were too virulent and the medication was ineffective. She passed away yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. It is now reported that the funeral will be held at 10:00 AM on the 15th of this month at the Wanguo Funeral Home on Jiaozhou Road, followed by burial at the Wanguo Public Cemetery on Hongqiao Road. Ms. Zhu Hu Binxia graduated from Wellesley College in the United States in 1913. After returning to China, she served enthusiastically in the fields of education, society, and charity in Ping, Qing, and Shanghai, and was highly respected by all walks of life. Now that the shocking news has arrived, everyone who hears it is deeply saddened.

He delivered an opening speech, detailing the importance of new medicines and stating that Central-Western Pharmacy's custom-made new drugs had long been renowned. Subsequently, Zhou Bangjun, nominated by the initiators, reported on the preparations, covering the following points: (1) The 45-year history of Central-Western Pharmacy's founding, (2) The difficulties in maintaining the company after Gongfa's bankruptcy, and (3) The current workforce of over 300 employees within the pharmacy, with over 2,000 special agents, reaching as far as Dihua in Xinjiang, covering almost the entire country. Following this, the articles of association were discussed, with drafter Shen Jiazhen, a certified public accountant, explaining them item by item. After passing, an election was held for seven directors and two supervisors, with Zhu Zengzong, Miao Zhijie, Geng Boyang, Zhu Xiaochun being nominated, Wang Moxian, Huang Qihua, Hu Dongbao, Mu Chunrong supervising the ballot counting, Zhou Wenji, Huang Jingwan, Zhou Shuku, Wu Zirang tallying the votes, and Wang Kaicun, Xia Wenhua, Zhao Jingyu, and Lu Chong writing the ballots. The elected candidates are listed as follows: Directors: Chu Minyi, Zhu Zengzong, Song Guobin, Wu Shaoting, Zhou Bangjun, Zhou Zhongying, and Fu Ruoyu; Supervisors: Mu Chunrong and Shao Fuzhanmei.

French Concession Public Health Department Adds Dental Clinic

Dr. Baode, Director of the Public Health Department of the French Concession, recognizing that the poor often lack the means to seek medical treatment, established a medical clinic last year. Those seeking treatment have praised its excellence, and its achievements are remarkable. Now, a dental clinic has been added to the clinic at 630 Beile Road, with the opening scheduled for the 14th of this month. Every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, from 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM, individuals can visit free of charge. However, it is still limited to poor residents within the French Concession who lack the means to pay. It is said that the internal equipment is very new and innovative, truly good news for the poor.

Its content is rich and its arguments are fair, which has made it popular among readers. Therefore, the first issue was reprinted after publication, and there is still a situation of supply falling short of demand. It is now heard that issue number 202 has been published, containing major works such as "Critique of Professor Tao Xisheng's and Professor Luo Longji's Anti-Japanese Theories" by Chen Zhigao, "Notes on Post-War and Eternal Peace" by Chen Gaoyong, and "The Way Out in Difficulties" by Sun Xiaoyang, as well as research materials on the railway in the Eastern Provinces, making it a must-read publication for everyone in the anti-Japanese movement. It is heard that the third issue of the publication will be a special New Year's issue, filled with famous authors and a wide variety of content. Presales are extremely popular.

Minli Weekly: The eighth issue of Minli Weekly has been published. In addition, the novel "Lone Army" and Mo Qian's rabbit novel are both excellent works.

Modern Children's Bi-Monthly: In order to improve children's reading and reduce the burden on elementary school students, the Sima Road Modern Bookstore has established the "Modern Children's Reading Club," expanding the children's reading movement. In addition to publishing the "Modern Children's Series," it has also launched the "Modern Children" bi-monthly, hiring Song Yi as the editor-in-chief. Contributors such as Zhao Zhishun, Qian Juntao, Jiang Hengnu, Xie Liuyi, and Li Baiying are all well-known children's literature writers in the literary world. The illustrations are all made by children's painting expert Mi Wenhuan. It is known that the first, second, and third issues of the first volume were published simultaneously yesterday. The content is simple, and there are many illustrations. The long comic strip story "Brother Elephant" is a special feature of the publication. The content is suitable for elementary school students in grades 3, 4, 5, and 6. The actual price per book is six cents, and the annual subscription for 24 books, including postage, is one yuan and forty-four cents. Anyone who joins the Bureau's Children's Reading Club will receive a free annual subscription. The annual membership fee is two yuan for local residents and two yuan and thirty cents for out-of-town residents.

Giant Sound Movie "Silver Han Shuangxing" Premieres Today

The musical and dance sound movie "Silver Han Shuangxing," starring Violet Kam and Jin Yan, is scheduled to premiere at the Nanjing Grand Theatre starting today. The film is based on the original novel by famous novelist Zhang Genshui, depicting the tragic love story of two brilliant stars on the screen, as well as the struggle between love and etiquette. The scenery is magnificent, and the talent is abundant. Violet Kam's pure singing and beautiful dancing are intoxicating, while Jin Yan's performance is profound and moving. The Nanjing Grand Theatre, which has never screened domestic films before, is making an exception for this film, indicating that it must have considerable value.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the Yangtze River Basin is cloudy and very cold, with fog in some areas. There is rain or snow in the Yellow Sea, and rain in the area south of Ma'an Island. There are extremely strong seasonal winds from the northwest to northeast along the coast of the entire country. The winds are especially strong in the Taiwan Strait. In addition, the temperature in Shanghai in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday did not reach a high or low record due to weather changes. The highest on the same day last year was 61.7 degrees, and the lowest was 39.0 degrees.

Reader's Correspondence

Student Strike, Suicide: Luo Dafan

Since the violent Japanese occupation of the three northeastern provinces, patriotic sentiment has been high both inside and outside China. Student enthusiasm is even greater, with petitions, demonstrations, and propaganda occurring almost daily. This kind of patriotic spirit is a support for diplomacy and the soul of the nation, and is truly commendable. However, the all-too-frequent occurrence of student strikes, without weighing the importance of the matter, leaves the reporter pacing anxiously, unable to remain silent. In recent years, laborers around the world, oppressed by capitalism, have resorted to strikes as a weapon of resistance, aiming to harm the enemy (capitalists) and seek their own interests. Students have followed suit, often using strikes as a tool to resist all enemies, forming a habit that is difficult to reverse. This has led to a decline in the efficiency of school education, and the nation's plan for cultivating talent has also suffered a great blow. If this continues, it will be difficult to resist the invasion of the violent Japanese and to ensure the nation's eternal survival. The reporter has worked in education for many years and has witnessed the reasons for school strikes over the past two decades. These can be summarized as follows: (1) Regarding the students themselves, if their demands are not met, such as regarding curriculum, facilities, or poor teachers, they often resort to strikes as a last resort. (2) Regarding the school itself, if the school is reorganized, students may support or reject it based on emotions, and sometimes unscrupulous teachers use students to consolidate their positions. (3) Regarding domestic politics, in recent years, the political situation has been volatile, and disappointed dignitaries or ambitious politicians often take advantage of opportunities to incite student unrest as a means of overthrowing the government. (4) Regarding diplomacy, students have repeatedly used the weapon of strikes, and over time, they have become accustomed to it. Therefore, when foreign aggression occurs or negotiations fail, they also resort to strikes, believing that it can prompt the authorities to reflect. The response is universal, and they are not ashamed of it. Considering the above, it is well known that while workers' strikes against capitalists cause some damage to social production, they are not contradictory to the goal of maintaining their own interests. Students who strike due to their own interests may be able to compensate for their losses with the results they achieve. However, those who are used to maintain the positions of teachers or serve as sacrifices for ambitious individuals are losing the precious time of hundreds, thousands, or even millions of people, while the beneficiaries are only the rights of one or two private individuals, which has nothing to do with the students themselves. In retrospect, the students must regret their actions, realizing that they were not worthwhile. If the nation is in danger and a strong neighbor is rampant, it is the duty of soldiers to go to the front line to kill the enemy and defend the country. It is the responsibility of the people to do their best to support the army in terms of supplies and the transportation of weapons. As for students, in addition to making efforts to promote patriotism within a reasonable time, holding demonstrations to express public opinion, their main task should still be to intensify their studies in order to prepare to take on the important responsibility of saving the country in the future. The previous cart has overturned, so the following cart should be cautious. Accumulate strength and strive to make persistent efforts. This is the certain process of saving the country, and it is also the duty of each of us, which cannot be surpassed and must be chosen carefully. The diligence and efforts of our young students are enough to establish prestige and deter the enemy. Moreover, the Japanese invasion is happening without the need for any arrows or bullets, as if entering an uninhabited area. This is an unprecedented shame in our history, and anyone with blood in their veins would be heartbroken. The reporter believes that national salvation movements can be divided into different tasks and do not need to be forced. We should focus on practice and avoid empty rhetoric, understand the true situation of the enemy and ourselves, and consider the needs of the front line. Those who are eager to advance can organize volunteer armies and defend the country with weapons, which is commendable. Those who persevere can bury themselves in books and study the classics to develop grand strategies, which is also not blameworthy. Therefore, it is my opinion that young students should each follow their own aspirations and expand their abilities, without the need for a nationwide strike, but rather express their patriotism and loyalty in practice. If we endure hardship and bide our time, planning to destroy Wu in ten years, we can defeat the enemy without much effort. However, if we abandon our studies due to foreign aggression and place the fate of countless young people in the country on a single gamble, then we are abandoning the fundamental and pursuing the superficial, and the soldiers will be defeated before the battle. Our morale will be weak, and our spirit will be empty. Moreover, our people are currently working hard to sever economic ties in order to resist the violent Japanese, so that Japan will suffer material losses and reduce its combat power. If our young students all engage in a long-term strike, then we will first suffer an incalculable spiritual loss, which is tantamount to using the weapon of strikes to commit suicide, causing no harm to the enemy and only benefiting them. The Japanese will laugh at us. I hope that our beloved millions of young students will carefully consider their choices, not be bound by old habits, and act rashly.

(Response: In various places, young people have held petitions, marches, and propaganda work related to diplomatic issues, resulting in strikes and even nationwide strikes. This is a heartbreaking matter. The news refers to it as "suicide," which is indeed the case. The purpose of suicide is to arouse the other party's awareness. If this effect cannot be achieved, is it not even more unjust? Ultimately, it is hoped that the government will not create reasons for strikes. Diplomatic policies should be based on public opinion, and all declarations must be substantial and long-lasting. Within the realm of possibility, we should do our best to inform the people of the changes in diplomacy and the difficulties in dealing with them. At the same time, public administration should be transparent, so that people have the opportunity to participate in politics and have freedom of assembly and speech. If we can do this, even if someone incites student unrest, they will find it difficult to do so, and there will be no need to do so. This is the only way to fundamentally solve the problem of student unrest.)

Letter

To the esteemed editor, I have read the news in your newspaper's local Shanghai news column yesterday, which stated that "Jiang Xueqian, a representative of Zhongda University, was injured in a beating." This is quite shocking. Upon investigation, Xueqian has not left the capital in recent days. The Anti-Japanese Association of our school does not have Xueqian participating, so there is no way for him to represent the association, let alone represent the association at a joint anti-Japanese conference of various universities in Shanghai, resulting in being beaten. The information in your newspaper is clearly a mistake in the name of another person. In addition to publishing a notice in various newspapers in the capital to clarify this, I am writing to you specifically to request a correction. To the Shenbao Newspaper Office, Jiang Xueqian, December 11th.

Book Reviews

World Financial Situation (Continued) Edited by Zhu Binyuan of Nancin

In the world financial market, the so-called gold price or silver price refers to the ratio between gold and silver. However, in countries with a gold standard, the fluctuations in silver are calculated based on the gold standard currency. The buying and selling of silver is no different from other commodities, so it can be said that there is only a silver price, and no so-called gold price. As for the extraordinary prevalence of copper subsidiary coins in our country's society, and the existence of a separate market price between them and the main currency, the silver price in the British and American financial markets has a dual meaning in our country's market. This is the so-called "gold-silver ratio." Here, the editor presents the situation of the past decade with accurate proportions, so that readers can understand the truth of the matter. In the present day of soaring gold prices and falling silver prices, this "gold-silver ratio" must be given importance.

International exchange is the most common means of clearing international debts, so the fluctuations in exchange rates are based on the changes in international lending relationships. There are many factors that create lending relationships, such as foreign trade, foreign debt principal and interest, freight, insurance, tariffs, overseas remittances from overseas Chinese, overseas business expenses, and salaries of foreign envoys. Of these, trade and foreign debt are the most important. The editor elaborates on this in the "Exchange Rate" section in an extremely clear manner.

Chapter Three: "Increases and Decreases in Cash Reserves and Paper Currency Circulation and Their Impact." Cash reserves and paper currency circulation describe the period when the European war was in full swing, when countries, in order to prevent cash outflows, declared a gold embargo on the one hand, and concentrated cash in the central bank or treasury on the other, resulting in a daily increase in reserves. After the war, the consolidation of the monetary system made this concentration even more necessary. Judging from the figures of the past decade, there has been a "soaring" trend. Secondly, there is the impact of the increase and decrease of gold reserves and paper currency on interest rates and prices, which is undoubtedly very detrimental to our country's market. Because when gold reserves change, the first thing that changes is the interest rate, followed by the exchange rate. When paper currency changes, the first thing that changes is the price of goods, followed by the exchange rate. China previously adopted the silver standard, so this point is also very important.

Chapter Four: "The Situation of Central Banks in Various Countries." This is very sufficient to provide reference for the study of banking. (1) The United States: Federal Reserve Bank (2) France: Bank of France. The biggest event in the financial aspect of France was the reform of the monetary system, because since the suspension of cash payments in the previous period, the value of the franc had plummeted. After much effort to rectify the situation, stability was restored in the previous year. (3) Germany: National Bank. Germany's economic situation was still good due to the favorable conditions of the year XX. After that, it gradually declined. Several industries raised domestic prices in order to reduce export prices, which greatly reduced the purchasing power of the domestic market. These all have the national bank's treasury. (4) Italy: Bank of Italy. (5) Japan: Bank of Japan. The editor has provided extremely detailed tables and explanations for these, which are very valuable for assistance.

Today's world is a world of economic competition. The rise and fall of national fortunes, the well-being of the people, and the prosperity of the country often depend on the strength of its economic power. Therefore, if we want to understand this point, we must first have a glimpse of the world's financial situation. Then, Mr. Zhu's book is worthy of our attention.

The Purpose and Organization of the League of Nations by Gao Wei

Translated and edited by Jiang Genyuan

This book collects all the materials on the League of Nations and narrates them in a concise style. We feel that although the League of Nations seems to be monopolized by ambitious people, we should not stand among the exploited masses and seek temporary peace. We must study the root cause and then prescribe the right medicine. As for this book's introduction to the League of Nations, it takes a completely faithful attitude. During this excitement about the Eastern Provinces Incident, everything is not discussed for the time being, but we will study its actual content, which is not without meaning.

This book is divided into four parts: Part 1: League of Nations Covenant, Part 2: Organization of the League of Nations, Part 3: Independent Organizations, and Part 4: Harmony, Continuity, and Development.

The first section discusses the interdependence of modern countries. We know that the fear of war among European countries has been deeply rooted in people's hearts since the 19th century. It was not until the Hague Conference in 1907 that the embryo of an organized system of national defense arbitration was produced, but it was destroyed by the tragedy of 1914. After the war, US President Wilson drafted a general outline of the League of Nations plan, as well as the peace treaty.
